Current Commentary

The Cause and Effect of the US Democratic Party's Abandonment of the Philippine Islands 　Heng 19

Of recent international events, two are most worthy of world attention. (1) The exchange of notes between the US and Japan. (2) The United States' permission for the Philippine Islands to become independent. The reason is that these two actions by the United States have a great impact on the situation in the Pacific. However, the former issue has already been discussed in detail in this newspaper and can be temporarily set aside. Here, the cause and effect of the latter issue will be presented. The US abandonment of the Philippine Islands does not seem to be related to our country in reality. At the same time, it is not completely without room for maneuver. We do not need to pay too much attention to it. However, in order to carefully examine the international situation, seize opportunities, and take advantage of the situation to ensure our territorial sovereignty, we must not ignore it.

The question of Philippine independence has been unresolved in the United States for more than thirty years. When it was transferred from Spanish hands to the US territory, the two major political parties in the US already had differing opinions. The Republican Party believed that if the Philippine Islands were under US control, it could be freed from Spanish tyranny and obtained by other powers. In fact, its intention was to strengthen the position of the United States in the Far East and curb the powers' coveting of China at that time. John Hay's Open Door Policy of equal opportunity was established after the US Republican government acquired the Philippine Islands. As for the policy of the Democratic Party, it was different. Therefore, when the US Navy attacked and captured the Philippine Islands, the Democratic Party not only did not take pride in it, but also denounced it as an "act of imperialism." When the Philippine Islands were officially ceded, the Democratic Party advocated making it independent. It believed that the US capture of the Philippine Islands was to save the Filipinos from misery, so it should not be taken as its own. If it were, it would be replacing violence with violence, which would be contrary to the original intention. There were deep reasons why the Democratic Party was so generous at that time. One thing that can be briefly mentioned is that since the North-South War, political power has often been in the hands of the Republican Party. At that time, American industry was developing rapidly and urgently needed to expand outward. The Republican Party, which was often in power, represented the interests of big industrialists and vigorously sought to expand its power in the East. The seizure of Pacific islands was all achieved during this period. However, it did not pay much attention to domestic affairs and often obstructed the revival of the Democratic Party. The Democratic Party was devastated during the North-South War and oppressed after the North-South War. It had been in opposition for a long time and had experienced many setbacks. The combination of these two factors led to its policy focusing on improving domestic affairs and ignoring the expansion of foreign power. It also said that the more victories and captures the ruling party had abroad, the more oppressive it would be at home. As a result, the Democratic Party's consistent policy of abandoning the Philippine Islands for the past thirty years was formed.

Commentators often say that the way of diplomacy is constantly changing and only looks at profit. However, this statement is only a superficial view. Taking the US abandonment of the Philippine Islands as an example, there are many reasons for it. In simple terms, first, it is the traditional policy of the party. Second, it is the economic reason. Third, it is the racial reason. Fourth, it is the deep fear of triggering a war between Japan and the United States. Let's talk about them separately.

It is obvious that we regard the US permission for the Philippine Islands to become independent as an action of the Democratic Party. First, the Democratic Party has always opposed the cession of the Philippine Islands from beginning to end. Second, every time a Democratic president is elected or the number of congressional seats increases, a Philippine independence bill is proposed. For example, in the past thirty years, there have been two periods when the US Democratic Party was in power. One was the Wilson era, and the other was the recent Roosevelt era. The Philippine independence bill could be passed without hindrance only during these two periods. Outside of these periods, even if there were proposals, it would be difficult to pass them. In total, the US Congress passed three Philippine independence bills during these two periods. (1) The Jones Act of Philippine Independence in 1916, which allowed the Philippine Islands to become independent once it had a strong government. It was approved by Wilson. When Wilson retired in 1920, he gave a farewell speech to Congress, recognizing that the time for Philippine independence had matured and urging immediate fulfillment of the promise. (2) The Hawes-Cutting Act at the end of 1932. At that time, the Democratic Party had a majority in both the Senate and the House of Representatives due to the 1930 elections, so it could be passed smoothly. Although the Democratic Party had won the presidential election at that time, President Hoover was still in office, so it was vetoed by Hoover. However, Congress had already fallen into the hands of the Democratic Party, and the president was powerless. Therefore, this bill finally became law. (3) Because the Philippine Congress opposed the Hawes-Cutting Act, Roosevelt asked both houses to reconsider it, and the Tydings-McDuffie Act of today was passed. The reason why this bill could be passed smoothly should be the power of the Democratic Party. We can see the partisan division in the US Congress today, and there is no need to doubt it. The Democratic Party actually occupies 313 seats out of the 435 seats in the House of Representatives. The Republican Party only occupies 117 seats. The Democratic Party actually occupies 60 seats out of the 96 seats in the Senate. The Republican Party only occupies 35 seats. The Democratic Party occupies such a large majority in Congress, and it can do everything freely. Therefore, the US permission for the Philippine Islands to become independent today is actually a manifestation of the US Democratic Party's implementation of its traditional policy and cannot be regarded as an action specifically to avoid Far Eastern disputes.

However, this matter was not only promoted by the traditional policy of one party, but also by economic, racial, and other reasons. If the Philippine Islands are not independent, their sugar and other products imported into the US will not be subject to import taxes, which will affect the business of sugar manufacturers in their own country. At the same time, if the Philippine Islands are not independent, Filipinos entering the US will not be restricted like other Asians, which may also affect the lives of American workers. Moreover, the Philippine Islands are 3,000 nautical miles from Honolulu and more than 5,000 nautical miles from San Francisco. It is too prominent and a major weakness in national defense. Therefore, commentators often say that the US ownership of the Philippine Islands is not only insufficient to enhance the US position in the Far East, but also enough to reveal its strategic shortcomings. If Japan provokes the US and attacks this weakness, the US will not be able to avoid war with Japan today. In addition, the coastline of the Philippines is more than 11,000 miles long, and the construction of fortresses, naval ports, and defense projects is extremely costly. At the Washington Conference in 1922, the reason why the US made concessions to Japan and stopped the construction of defense projects on the Philippine Islands was because the expenditure was too great. With the current economic decline of the United States, it is wise to abandon the Philippine Islands. Therefore, the US action on the Philippine Islands this time can also be regarded as a strategic retreat in advance and even as an expression of not wanting to go to war with Japan.

The above are all the reasons for the US abandonment of the Philippine Islands. Except for the last one, it can be said that it has little relationship with the Sino-Japanese problem in the Far Eastern incident. However, the impact is actually not completely unrelated. First, this action by the United States can somewhat reduce its prestige in the Far East and increase Japan's arrogance in doing whatever it wants. However, it is an exaggeration to say that Japan will have no constraints from now on. First, the 12-year period gives the US plenty of room for maneuver. Second, at the next Pacific Conference, the US, Russia, France, the Netherlands, and other countries may not support the US to ensure the neutrality of the Philippine Islands or even restrict Japan's actions in the Far East. Third, if the Pacific Conference fails, the US will still have ample time to prepare for sanctions against Japan. Fourth, the US House of Representatives is re-elected every two years, the Senate is re-elected one-third every two years, and the President is re-elected every four years. Therefore, the Republican Party has plenty of opportunities to regain power within 12 years. Therefore, whether the Philippine Islands can become independent within 12 years and whether the US Army and Navy can withdraw completely within the stipulated period are all unknown questions. Therefore, the people of the country do not need to worry too much about the US expression of abandoning the Philippine Islands today. What is needed is that we should have extremely careful and thorough preparations at the next Pacific Conference.

US Naval Bill Passed by Congress and Approved by the President Becomes Law 20

Only Building Ships Within the Scope of the Treaty

Roosevelt Hopes for International Disarmament

(Washington) President Roosevelt recently signed the Vinson Naval Bill, which stipulates the construction of 102 ships to the extent permitted by the naval treaty, and 1,184 aircraft. After being passed by the House of Representatives, the Senate added two amendments requiring that the profits obtained by private contractors for shipbuilding projects should not exceed 10%, and that one-quarter of the more than 1,000 aircraft should be built by the government itself. However, this was rejected by the House of Representatives. The Senate finally passed the original bill of the House of Representatives. Today, Roosevelt also signed a note explaining that the Vinson Law only allows shipbuilding in principle. As for the actual construction, it depends on the availability of funds. The President also said that he supports new naval reductions at the 1935 Naval Conference. (Havas dispatch on the 27th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt, in a letter attached to the Vinson Naval Bill, explained that this bill only allows the construction of the US Navy within the scope of the treaty, rather than building more warships. The authorities still take the policy of supporting continued reductions in naval armaments. The President also stated, "I hope that the naval conference to be held in 1935 can extend the existing restrictions and agree to greater reductions." It is reported that the Vinson Naval Proposal stipulates an expenditure of 500 million yuan for the construction of warships and aircraft. It was passed by the Senate on March 6, with some amendments attached, and then sent to the House of Representatives for reconsideration. However, the House of Representatives rejected the amendments. This bill is now returned to the Senate in order to reconcile the differences between the two houses. (Reuters dispatch on the 27th)

(Washington) The contents of the warship construction bill signed by the President today are as follows: (1) Total expenditure of 500 million yuan to 750 million yuan. (2) Period of seven years. (3) Types and numbers of warships to be built: 66 destroyers, 32 submarines, 4 cruisers, 1,140 aircraft. (4) Construction expenditure must be approved by the Budget Bureau. (Dentsu dispatch on the 27th)

(Washington) President Roosevelt has signed the Vinson Naval Bill today, and the United States can build two light cruisers, totaling 17,100 tons, one aircraft carrier of 15,000 tons, and several submarines, totaling 36,590 tons. The first to be built are 12 torpedo boats and 6 submarines. In addition, the regular budget stipulates the construction of one battlecruiser and three light cruisers, and funds are allocated from the public works expenditure item to build two aircraft carriers, one battlecruiser, three light cruisers, four submarines, twenty torpedo boats, and two gunboats. (Havas dispatch on the 27th)

Russian Newspaper Comments on US-Japan Exchange of Notes Showing Increasingly Sharp Conflicts in the Pacific 21

US Does Not Abandon Position Operated for Forty Years

Japan Prepares for Military Action on the Asian Continent

(Moscow) Pravda commented on the exchange of notes between Japanese Foreign Minister Hirota and US Secretary of State Hull. The newspaper pointed out that the Japanese press generally regarded this exchange of notes as "Hirota's victory" and said that Hirota had repeatedly stated that he would try to improve US-Japan relations in order to alleviate the political isolation in the external world after his invasion of China. "Japan is trying to neutralize one side of the front line (that is, the United States) so that it can feel at ease and further occupy the Asian continent. At the same time, in order to 'restore the traditional friendship between Japan and the United States,' it proposed that the United States recognize 'Manchukuo,' allow China to withdraw from the League of Nations, and the United States abolish the Japanese Immigration Law. The most requested thing is the equality of the land and sea military strength of the two countries. Japan also believes that it is necessary for the world to recognize it as a strong country to stabilize 'the East,' that is to say, what Tokyo thinks is right cannot be hindered by others. On the Japanese side, it has tried its best to express its willingness to conclude an arbitration treaty with the United States, establish neutral zones in the Pacific, and recognize the inviolability of the 'Open Door' principle. However, as the experience of Manchuria proves, these doors have been occupied by the Japanese, and even good American capitalists have not been able to enter." The newspaper further stated, "It is natural for Tokyo to prepare to negotiate with the United States at the above-mentioned price. Japanese imperialism obviously wants to rely on Hirota's letter to Hull to discover what it can hope for and what it needs to fear. As for the United States, which has been painstakingly managing to consolidate its position in the Pacific for forty years, how can it give up what Tokyo wants without bloodshed? Japan's diplomatic activities can only show the increasingly sharp imperialist conflicts in the Pacific and the enthusiastic work carried out by the Japanese diplomatic community to prepare for military action on the Asian continent." (TASS dispatch on the 27th)

(Tokyo) Foreign Minister Hirota intends to fully mobilize the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and overseas envoys, and Japan intends to automatically launch activities to major countries. Listen to direct reports on the recent situation and consult on policies and attitudes. (Dentsu dispatch on the 28th)

India Raises Tariffs on Cotton Textiles

He said that although the Governor of Hong Kong had guaranteed that British water cement would be purchased as much as possible, in fact, among the 42 public buildings in Hong Kong, 30 used Japanese cement, the local product was used in a certain number of structures and the hybrid variant in two. The Colonial Secretary replied that, in general, colonial governments are willing to use British goods as much as possible. As for the matters questioned by Mr. Havas, he did not know, but promised to investigate. (Reuters dispatch on the 27th)

(Osaka) The tariff on cotton interlock fabric is as high as twelve annas per pound. The telegram from the Japan-India Association has given a great shock to the parties concerned. It is found that most of the interlock fabrics currently exported to India weigh one and a half to three and a half pounds per dozen, and the tariff in Bombay is 24 annas, which is equivalent to 18% ad valorem. Therefore, there is no other way to completely eliminate Japan's interlock fabric exports to India. The union of this industry in Japan recently sent representatives to Tokyo to make representations to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, urging it to find ways to prevent further increases. However, the consultations this time will certainly be a strong foundation for negotiations. I hope that an agreement will be established in the near future. (Jiji dispatch on the 27th)

Effectiveness of Anglo-Russian Trade Agreement 27

(London) Judging from the statistics for February recently published, the effectiveness of the Anglo-Russian Trade Agreement is quite obvious. Soviet Russia's purchase of British goods was 34% more than in February last year. The machines purchased were £64,075, compared with £35,127 last year; woven fabrics were £17,155, compared with £206 last year; rubber was £189,325, compared with £6,097 last year; tea was £175,834, compared with £32,864 last year. It is estimated that Russia purchased approximately £900,2863, compared with £673,400 last year. The number of ships leased by Soviet Russia from Britain has also increased, reaching 208,000 tons last month. (Reuters dispatch on the 28th)

Gambling Should Be Prohibited 28

Animal Racing and Lottery Tickets are All Within the Limits

British Parliament to Introduce Bill

(London) The government's bill to restrict gambling will be submitted to the House of Lords for its first reading tonight. The purpose of this bill is to amend the laws on gambling. Anyone under the age of seventeen is not allowed to participate in gambling such as horse racing and dog racing, and the issuance of lottery tickets in the UK is prohibited. Anyone who has lottery tickets in their possession for sale or promotion will be considered to be violating the law, except for those who do not use money as prizes. Violators will be fined for the first offense and imprisoned for repeated offenses. (Reuters dispatch on the 27th)

Italy Promotes After-Work Sports

Security Guarantees Persist and Do Not Loosen

Germany's Eastern Policy

Poland Uneasy

(Warsaw) French Foreign Minister Barthou arrived in the capital of Belgium this afternoon. His visit to Poland will be on April 22. Since then, France could no longer regard Poland as an ally that only added to the burden. Negotiations on Security Issues Between Britain and France 33

A tendency to establish partial agreements

The General Commission on Disarmament will postpone its meeting

(London) Yesterday, the Cabinet Committee on Disarmament met to study the French government's reply of March 17 regarding the disarmament issue. It was believed that the French government intended to divide security measures into two types: one for the implementation of future disarmament conventions and the other for general security. As reported in yesterday's telegram, French Ambassador to Britain, Corbin, verbally explained to Foreign Secretary Simon the interpretation of the security measures for the implementation of the disarmament convention mentioned in the French reply of March 17. Further exchange of views will follow. While British officials are not overly optimistic about this matter, they believe there are satisfactory reasons. In any case, Foreign Secretary Simon will report the information he has obtained to the Cabinet meeting tomorrow. He will likely meet with Henderson, the chairman of the Disarmament Conference, immediately. The meeting of the Bureau's minority committee, originally scheduled for April 10, may also be postponed. Before the Cabinet meeting, influential opinions are divided into two factions: one advocates that Britain and France discuss security measures for the implementation of the disarmament convention, and the other believes that after the Disarmament Conference loses credibility and issues a declaration, they should be pragmatic and quickly strengthen national defense. Currently, the first faction still prevails, but if current efforts still fail, the second faction's opinion will inevitably gain the upper hand. The current efforts seem to be trending towards the establishment of partial agreements, as reported by this newspaper yesterday. That is, if security measures for the implementation of the disarmament convention cannot be made effective worldwide, an agreement should be established only for Britain and its closest neighbors, and less coercive measures should be adopted for countries outside this scope. The reason for this trend is the strong attitude of the United States. When criticizing France in its reply to Britain on disarmament, the US President stated that if international issues are discussed and consultation conventions are concluded, the United States is willing to participate, but if it is forced to use force to resolve any international disputes, the United States cannot recognize it. Amidst the divergent opinions of various factions, we have discovered a thought, that is, the British generally believe that the current issue is related to the security of Britain itself. British people currently regard the air force led by German Aviation Minister Göring as equivalent to the armored ships commanded by Admiral Tirpitz of the German Navy before the European War. Therefore, the current hope of the British people is to protect national security at the lowest cost and avoid all dangers. Understanding this, we can easily understand why Britain's opinion on the disarmament issue may change but also faces difficulties. (Havas News Agency, 27th)

Two Types of Guarantees 34

(London) According to sources here, the negotiations between Britain and France on national security may have significant developments since British Ambassador to France, Corbin, spoke with British Foreign Secretary Simon last night. It is said that Lord John had previously asked Ambassador Corbin to present three special questions regarding this matter to the French government, and the French response to these questions was conveyed by Ambassador Corbin to Lord John last night. The three questions are listed in order as follows:

(1) In the event of a dispute between the two countries, will France provide an executive guarantee or an ordinary guarantee? These are two different types of facts. According to Ambassador Corbin, France has recognized the theoretical difference between an executive guarantee and an ordinary guarantee, but in practice, it does not make this distinction, because once a treaty is violated, it will inevitably involve force. At this time, it is important to show that our treaty countries approve of the executive guarantee and the ordinary guarantee.

(2) If France has determined the difference between an executive guarantee and an ordinary guarantee, then what kind of guarantee does France want in two different situations? According to Ambassador Corbin, France's response to this point was very tactful and questioned what kind of guarantee Britain was willing to offer.

(3) Does France want a territorial guarantee system or an ordinary guarantee system?

According to Ambassador Corbin, France agrees to a territorial guarantee agreement, and France may even question what scope of agreement Britain is willing to suggest. (National Telegram, 28th)

Germany Builds Large Airship 37

Four and a Half Times Larger Than Zeppelin

Can Accommodate Fifty Passengers

Friedrichshafen, Germany Today, the construction details of Germany's new passenger airship, named "LZ129" (Airship 129), were announced by the Zeppelin factory authorities. The airship is expected to be completed this summer. All the equipment inside is larger than the original "Graf Zeppelin". The "Graf Zeppelin" airship has one passenger cabin, two dining rooms, and several bedrooms, accommodating 24 passengers. The newly built "Airship 129" has two passenger cabins and dining rooms, 25 bedrooms, and can accommodate 50 beds. The total indoor area available for passengers has increased by at least four and a half times. Each room is divided into a dining room, writing room, reading room, and smoking room, and smoking will especially be welcomed by passengers in the future, because passengers on the "Graf Zeppelin" were prohibited from smoking. The equipment used in this ship is of the Diesel type, with a total power of 4,400 horsepower, and it uses heavy oil as fuel, so the risk of fire is unlikely to occur. (National Telegram, 27th)

Austria's Price for Suppressing the Riot 38

Socialist Party Still Waiting for the Opportunity

Austrian Emblem Will Be Changed to a Double-Headed Eagle

Vienna In recent days, the Socialist Party's propaganda activities in Vienna have become active again. Party members are said to have transported leaflets from the Czech Republic and distributed them everywhere, persuading workers to be patient and wait for the opportunity, and advising them to pay attention to the "Kranas" newspaper (formerly the Socialist Party's newspaper, now taken over by the government) and government radio broadcasts, and not to be misled. (Havas News Agency, 28th)

Vienna According to sources here, the Austrian government will change its current republican emblem based on the new Austrian constitution and adopt the "double-headed eagle" of the Habsburg era to replace it, because the current "hammer and sickle symbol of the Marx Republic" has a similar connotation to the symbol of the Communist Party. It is also reported that the Austrian government will follow Germany and designate May 1 as a "national holiday." (National Telegram, 28th)

France Implements Administrative Reduction 39

Abolishing the System of Holding Concurrent Positions

Eighty Thousand Civil Servants Retire

(Paris) Following the Nanjing method, the French government decided today to abolish the system of holding concurrent positions, and decided to order 80,000 civil servants to retire and no longer supplement them. It is expected that a clear order will be issued within a few days. According to reliable sources, government salaries are about to be reduced, and it is estimated that this method can save 500 million francs, because the government urgently needs 4 billion francs to balance its budget. Although the system of holding concurrent positions has not been completely abolished in Nanjing, it is expected that the French government will resolutely implement its new resolution even if it encounters resistance from those involved. Some parties say that salary reductions and layoffs may cause disturbances, but the government seems to have prepared everything, and party leaders everywhere have also adopted measures to maintain public security and order. Prime Minister Doumergue's position is currently very stable. The National Veterans Federation, which has 3 million members, has decided to participate in national political life and support the Prime Minister. Veterans are very powerful. With the Prime Minister's assistance, he can prevent the occurrence of new disturbances. The government's decision to lay off staff will naturally cause fierce verbal battles in the Chamber of Deputies. If Doumergue's plan to balance the budget fails, then another change in the French government is inevitable. (Reuters, 27th)

The White House Vetoes the Proposal to Increase Pensions for Officials 40

The House of Representatives Votes to Maintain the Original Proposal

The Fate of this Bill Depends on the Senate

(Washington) The bill to increase the amount of veteran support and subsidies had been passed by the Senate and the House of Representatives successively, but the President strongly opposed it and applied the veto power, sending the original bill back to Congress and refusing to promulgate it, and explaining the reasons for his veto in a message. After receiving the President's message, the House of Representatives again submitted the original bill for a vote. As a result, those who advocated maintaining the original bill and opposed the President's veto reached 301 votes, including 200 Democrats, 97 Republicans, and 4 Farmer-Labor Party members, which reached more than the legally required two-thirds majority. If the Senate also adopts the same attitude, the President's veto will be invalid. However, the situation in the Senate is currently unknown. In his message to Congress on this matter, Roosevelt vigorously stated that raising the salaries of officials by another level is, in his view, a matter of principle, not only related to government expenditures. When the country is engaged in economic recovery, he hopes that Congress can continue to cooperate with him. At present, there is more than one end that needs extraordinary expenditure. For example, agriculture needs relief, and farmers and owners have debts that cannot be repaid, and the government must have a way to help them. Millions of unemployed people must be given work. These are all unexpected burdens on the national treasury. Since expenditures increase, other government expenditures must be saved. This is a natural principle. The President also said that he expressed his sympathy for the officials, but the plight of millions of unemployed people is far more pitiful than that of the officials. In addition, there are injured veterans and those who are healthy. During service, there are those with upright conduct and those with misconduct. In principle, they should be distinguished, but Congress treats them equally and gives them all the right to enjoy support, which is completely unacceptable. (Havas News Agency, 27th)

Labor Unrest in the United States Rises and Falls 41

Riots and Strikes in Various Places

(Washington) The recent trend of labor unrest in the United States fluctuates. The public believes that the entire steel industry will follow the story of the McKinley Steel Company and increase the wages of workers to stabilize the workers' hearts. Although Federal Transportation Regulator Isven has not yet issued a declaration recently, he is still working hard today to mediate the dispute over wage cuts in the railway industry. In the flour mills in Cleveland, riots and strikes occur at the same time, and many workers have been arrested. A strike of 3,200 workers also occurred at the New York Shipbuilding Company in New Jersey. It is said that the strike was caused by opposition to the company's manipulation of labor unions and wages. Two cruisers and four destroyers being built by the US Navy have been forced to stop work as a result. In addition, 2,000 workers in an aircraft factory also went on strike demanding wage increases. The wave of strikes in the automobile industry has entered a peaceful area, because the dove of peace has come to Detroit and other automobile manufacturing centers. President Roosevelt's arbitration committee began mediating the labor unrest in the West Coast Wolf Blood Gate in San Francisco today. It is said that if the Wolf Blood Gate labor unrest is realized, the US Pacific shipping industry will be severely affected. (National Telegram, 27th)

Jiangnan Railway Company Contracts to Build the Kyoto Zhao Railway 50

Construction Cost is Approximately 30 Million

The Project is Carried Out in Five Sections

(Nanjing) In order to expand its railway business and connect the seven southeastern provinces, the Jiangnan Railway Company presented to and was approved by the Ministry of Railways to contract to build the Kyoto Zhao Railway, which starts from Nanjing and reaches Zhao'an on the border of Fujian and Guangdong. The entire route is about 1,200 kilometers long, passing through the five provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Zhejiang, Fujian, and Guangdong, crossing important mountains such as Huangshan, Tiantai, and Dayu. The construction is larger and more difficult than the Wuzha Railway. Its position in transportation is all the more necessary due to the difficulty of the construction. The interior of the five southeastern provinces is mostly mountainous, relying only on bamboo rafts traveling on rivers and streams. Products have no way to be transported out, and languages and cultures are mostly isolated. Now that it is connected, its benefits are several times greater than the Wuzha Railway. The estimated construction cost is 30 million yuan. The project is planned by Hong Shentong, the chief engineer of the Wuzha Railway. The entire route is divided into five sections for construction and five construction periods, namely (1) the Kyoto Wu section, (2) the Wu Sun section (Sunjiahe), (3) the Sun Jiang section (Jiangshan, Zhejiang), (4) the Jiang Yan section (Yanping, Fujian), and (5) the Yan Zhao section. After reaching Zhao'an, it is planned to extend the route to Guangzhou to realize the transportation plan for the five southeastern provinces. However, the subgrade of the second section between Wuhu and Sunjiabu will use the track currently built by the Wuzha Railway, so the construction of the second section can be saved. Only the four sections of Kyoto Wu and others are built on the entire route. The funding for the first phase of the project has been remitted from Shanghai, and construction will begin within five days. The original automobile route between Kyoto and Wu runs along the south bank of the Yangtze River, and is too curved and unsuitable for transportation. A new road will be built instead. The surveying team personnel are transferred from the Wuzha Railway and sent to the road for surveying, led by Survey Team Leader Wang. The Kyoto Wu section is mostly plains, making construction very easy. Among them, the Dahe River in Dangtu County will be connected by a three-hole iron bridge. It is expected to be completed and open to traffic by the end of June this year. Regarding the subgrade between Sunjiabu and Jiangshan, after passing Tunxi, it must pass through the mountains. Liu Yiyan, the director of the Anhui Construction Department, once served as the director of the Hangzhou-Jiangxi Railway Bureau and is familiar with the terrain of southern Zhejiang. He was recruited by Zhang Jingjiang, the general manager of the Jiangnan Railway Company, and arrived in Kyoto a few days ago to discuss everything. Sun Qiming and Xia Quanshou, two technicians sent by the Ministry of Railways to survey and verify the road work, have completed the survey and verification of the Wuwan section of the Wuzha Railway and are continuing to investigate in Xuancheng. Once the Kyowu section of the Kyosho Road is completed, the Ministry of Railways will handle joint transportation with the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Road and the Kyoto-Tianjin Road in order to facilitate transportation. The Huainan Railway on the north bank of the Yangtze River is sponsored by the Central Construction Committee, starting from the Luhe coal mine in Bengbu, west to Huaiyuan County, and reaching Yuxikou on the opposite bank of Wubu. The work has begun, and it is expected that Wuhu will become a water and land transportation center. (Special Telegram, 28th)

Gu Renfa Issues Statement on Li Shuyun Case 73

(Zhenjiang) Gu Renfa issued the following statement regarding the arrest of Li Shuyun: "While I was on official business in Jiangxi, an incident of resisting the surrender occurred at the Second Branch Bureau of the Wuxi Public Security Bureau. As a result, my wife Li Shuyun and her daughter were arrested. I am concerned that various sectors of society may not understand the truth, so I will briefly explain the process. In the spring of the 20th year of the Republic, I returned to my hometown to visit relatives. Due to disagreements with my previous wife Yun, we divorced through the mediation of relatives. Several months later, I remarried Li Shuyun. This time, while I was away on official business, she dared to go to Wuxi privately and instigated Liu Zhuomin to resist the surrender. Furthermore, according to reports from various parties, her mother and daughter have been using false names in Changsha to swindle money and engage in various illegal activities. Recently, the Wuxi Public Security Bureau found forged seals of my personal stamp in the suitcase of Liu's wife Li Rongzhen, which were stamped on the lower left corner of the official stationery used by the provincial government and provincial residence. The circumstances are particularly serious. I am inherently cautious and have been appointed to lead civil affairs, entrusted by the government and recognized by the chairman. I always strive to rectify discipline and eliminate corruption. Now that the Wuxi incident has revealed that my wife Shuyun is the main culprit, along with her various illegal activities, damaging personal reputation is a minor matter, but undermining national discipline is a major matter. At a time when we are vigorously promoting propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame and transforming customs, if the national law cannot be enforced among relatives, how can we rectify official norms and set an example for our colleagues? Such incidents are very common in our country's ancient and modern rule-of-law countries, where the law is valued over personal feelings. The media should be at the forefront of safeguarding the rule of law and provide accurate guidance. However, I am responsible for failing to manage my family properly and for misusing personnel and should request punishment to clarify my responsibility. As for Shuyun and her mother's actions of biting back in desperation and falsely accusing me of bigamy, this is a personal matter and has its own proper channels for resolution, and it is not related to the rectification of discipline by the government. " (Special dispatch, 28th)

(Zhenjiang) After returning to the province, Gu Renfa actively reorganized government affairs, such as planning to abolish the public security sub-bureaus in various counties, organizing a screening committee for public security bureau chiefs, and personally instructing his subordinates to strive to implement the New Life Movement. Reports of his resignation are inaccurate. Gu stated that he would not leave his post before the Li case comes to light. (Special dispatch, 28th)

Another Report on British Encroachment on Ban Hong 95

| Heaven-Given Treasures Have Already Been Exploited |

Beijing News: Regarding the British encroachment on the Ban Hong incident, the Yunnan Association in Beijing, in addition to petitioning the central government to negotiate with the British side through the government, has also established the Yunnan-Burma Border Demarcation Promotion Committee to study the border issue, hoping to contribute to and urge the government to reclaim sovereignty. Recently, the association has learned from reports from people in Ban Hong that although there are many records of the British military occupation of Ban Hong and the mining situation, there are still many omissions. The reports are more detailed and are recorded to provide references for those who are concerned. According to reports, British encroachment on Ban Hong has become a serious issue of unanimous concern throughout the country. However, the Ban Neng mentioned by the British side is very far from Ban Hong and cannot be discussed together. An on-site survey would make it clear. There was originally a large-scale silver factory there, which the British had coveted for a long time. This time, they occupied the mine by force, which was also expected. From Man E to Huiqin River, that is, the border between Yunnan and Burma, there are stone pillars, but the numbers are unclear. This stone pillar was originally in the Hubu boundary, 60 li away from here, and was secretly moved in by someone. From Hongyantou to Maliba Keyu City, it was occupied by the British in the 20th year of Guangxu and opened as a commercial port. The British changed it to Gogan County and appointed the old Yang Tusi as the county magistrate, which shows their deep intentions. The British also have postal, telegraph, school, church, and agency organs. Turning down to Xiushui Village, that is, the undetermined boundary, crossing the lower reaches of the Nanding River, to Gongmeng, from Menggang to Ban Hong, there are large bamboo forests and giant trees along the way, and silver factories, with Muslim natives interspersed. To Ban Neng, there are many metal mines, especially rich in silver mines. The natives used indigenous methods and Islam to mine them, which was quite effective. The British often used coercion and enticement to cause disputes between the natives and Muslims in order to profit from them. Fortunately, Muslim intellectuals stood up to mediate, and there was no fierce battle. However, after the turmoil, many natives avoided the chaos elsewhere. The British then implemented their colonial policy, making the natives mutually guarantee each other. For each household that came, they allocated a piece of land according to the number of people, loaned them 100 yuan, one cow, and one stone of grain, and ordered them to build thatched huts next to the fields for farming. As a result, 2,000 households were moved away. Passing through Pachang Mountain from Ban Neng, entering Gongmeng, and heading south, it is the savage land of Kun, located between the Gun, Lu, Nan, and Ban Rivers, shaped like a gourd, so it is also called the Gourd King Land, with five small tribes, each with a native king, with Nangun River Gongming Mountain as the gateway, about 900 li vertically and more than 2,000 li horizontally, with more than 20,000 households and more than 100,000 people. The territory is rich in minerals and products and is our southwest barrier. During the Qing Dynasty, Gong Ling once went to its territory, but since the traffic was blocked, no one has taken care of it since the Republic of China. The British then developed the ambition to invade, such as repairing roads, lending silver coins and cloth to the natives, or renting cattle and horses and distributing salt. Fortunately, the workers still know that there are Chinese and have not been completely occupied. To the west, crossing the Gunlu River from Mengyu to Mengwan, Mengying, Mengliang, Mengjie, and Mengyang, about 300 li, there is barren grass and smoke, sparsely populated. Arriving at Lashio, that is, the end of the British Burmese Railway, the British have opened it as a commercial port, where people from all over the world are mixed. There are many overseas Chinese from Guangdong and Sichuan and Yunnan. There are overseas Chinese schools and branches of the Chinese Nationalist Party. To Banghai and Nandulao Silver Factory, which was originally mined by the Chinese, it fell to the British in the 12th year of Guangxu. Now there is a railway directly to the mine, producing 2,000 tons of silver ore every day, which can refine 120 tons of silver and 800 tons of lead, with more than 30,000 workers, including more than 10,000 Chinese workers. In the past, because the Qing government could not manage it, they were willing to give way. What else can be said? The British occupation of Ban Hong this time was due to the fact that in the autumn of last year, the Yunnan Fu Dian Bank sent people to conduct a survey to engage in mining Ban Hong silver mines and was about to start planning to proceed, which was known to the British. They took preemptive action and sent workers to invade Ban Hong for mining this spring. The five Tusi of Shanghulu refused to accept this and rose up to argue, which led to the conflict. In order to protect the miners, the British sent 2,000 troops into the country to implement armed occupation, and the situation is serious. Neighboring counties such as Lancang and Zhenkang were shocked and reported to the Yunnan Provincial Government for a halt. The provincial government could not deal with it because it involved foreign affairs, and the situation became increasingly serious. At present, the natives and the British are fighting every day."

Japanese Exploit Chinese Traitors to Recruit Chinese Laborers 96

Chinese Laborers Recruited in Baoding Discovered

More Than 20,000 Chinese Laborers Transported to Rehe

Beiping Correspondence: After the fall of Rehe, the Japanese paid special attention to the construction of the province. They paid special attention to the construction of buildings, digging wells, and water conservancy projects. Recently, they have been exploiting Chinese traitors to recruit workers in various counties of Hebei Province. Last night, a batch of workers was discovered by the police in Baoding and were all detained. They will be sent back to their hometowns separately. According to people from Goryeoyoung, a certain Japanese merchant firm sent personnel to Goryeoyoung on the 15th of this month to set up a "Chinese Labor Collection and Transportation Office." Since the 18th, Japanese people have been leading Chinese farmers from Beiping to Goryeoyoung in an endless stream. They were transported in batches by heavy trucks to Gubeikou. According to Japanese businessman Sakata, a total of 20 trucks are used to transport goods between Goryeoyoung and Gubeikou. According to Chinese laborers who arrived there, they were recruited by Japanese people in Shandong and Hebei provinces, including Zhengding and Dingxian, under the guise of recruiting Chinese laborers. Their journey was from various places by train to Xizhimen Railway Station, then walking to Goryeoyoung, and then taking a bus to Rehe. However, the Japanese did not specify what kind of work they would be doing when they recruited them. In recent days, hundreds of Chinese laborers have arrived at Goryeoyoung from Beiping every day and have been transported away by the Japanese by truck. It is said that the total number of Chinese laborers recruited this time is about 20,000. (27th)

Gold and Silver 98

London Gold Price: Today (28th) is 136 shillings and 3 pence, a decrease of half a penny from yesterday.

New York Bar: Today (28th), the silver market in New York opened with stability and strength, but there were not many transactions. Merchants are now waiting for the trends of other markets and the news from Washington regarding the Veterans Bonus Bill and the Days Silver Bill. The market was silent throughout the morning, and the prices were equivalent to London.

Exchange Market 99

The opening exchange rate between the British and American currencies was $5.10, the same as yesterday's closing rate. Japanese Use Traitors to Recruit Chinese Laborers 104

Recruitment of Chinese Laborers in Baoding Discovered

Over 20,000 Chinese Laborers Transported to Jehol

Beiping Correspondence: After the fall of Jehol, the Japanese have paid special attention to construction projects in the province. In terms of military affairs, they are building houses in groups and focusing on ditch digging, well digging, and water conservancy projects. Recently, [persons named] Li and other traitors have been recruiting laborers in various counties of Hebei Province. Last night, a group in Baoding was discovered by the police, and all were detained and will be sent back to their hometowns. According to people from Gaoli Camp, a certain Japanese firm sent personnel to Gaoli Camp on the 15th of this month to set up a "Chinese Labor Collection and Transportation Office." Since the 18th, Japanese have been leading our farmers, one after another, from Ping to Gaoli Camp, and transporting them in batches by heavy trucks to Gubeikou. According to Sakata, a Japanese person in Gaoli Camp, a total of twenty trucks are used solely for transportation between Gaoli Camp and Gubeikou. After the Chinese laborers arrive at Gubeikou, they are transferred to Japanese military trucks and transported to Chengde. According to Chinese laborers who have arrived there, they were recruited from Zhengding, Dingxian, and other places in Shandong and Hebei provinces by the Japanese under the guise of recruiting Chinese people. Their route is to take trains from various places to Xizhimen Station, walk to Gaoli Camp, and then take trucks to Jehol. However, the Japanese did not specify what kind of work they would be doing when they recruited them. Every day, hundreds of Chinese laborers arrive in Gaoli Camp from Ping and are transported away by the Japanese in trucks. It is said that the total number of Chinese people recruited this time is about 20,000. (27th)

Qingdao: Traitorous Plot Exposed 105

Major Riot Scheduled

Dozens of Traitors Arrested

Confessions Indicate Japanese Instigation

Qingdao Correspondence: Qingdao is an important town in North China and the gateway to Shandong. The Japanese have long coveted it. Last year, when the war in North China had not yet stopped, Japanese puppets secretly sent ruffians to Qingdao to collude with local traitors in the hope of staging an incident. However, due to the tight defense of the city's military and police, the matter did not succeed. Currently, the Qingdao Match Company has suspended operations due to the unbearable burden of consolidated taxes, and various yarn factories are also laying off workers due to sluggish business. As a result, the number of newly unemployed people in the city has exceeded 10,000. The Japanese saw an opportunity and used unemployed workers to secretly plan to disrupt the city's security. The Public Security Bureau had long been aware of this, so it paid close attention to the actions of Japanese ruffians and idle individuals. On the afternoon of the 24th of this month, at about 2:00 PM, people were repeatedly seen entering and exiting the seaside park. The nearby guards suspected that these people were suspicious, so they reported to the General Bureau, which sent several detectives to investigate. By the time they arrived, three people were still in the park. They were immediately arrested and taken to the bureau for strict interrogation. According to Sun Zuochen, Hu Maoxiao, and a person surnamed Ge (name unknown), they were instigated by the Japanese to prepare for a major riot at 8:00 PM on the 24th to occupy Qingdao and then hoist a puppet flag. The riot plan was as follows: (1) It was stipulated that the uprising would take place at 8:00 PM on the 24th, with the blackout of city streetlights as the signal. (2) After the lights went out, more than 700 Japanese and Chinese people would simultaneously depart from the Japanese Daigong Company (location unknown). The Japanese would transport bullets in cars with Japanese flags. (3) Ten Japanese, all dressed in Chinese clothing and armed with guns, would travel back and forth to direct. The Chinese would each carry bombs, and every two people would seize a policeman's gun. (4) Three machine guns would surround the Public Security Bureau. (5) The puppet flag would be hoisted four hours after Qingdao was occupied. (6) If the Chinese military and police resisted and their forces were unable to withstand it, the Japanese would immediately remove their Chinese clothing and change into Japanese clothing. (7) If Han Fuju's troops moved east, they would use landmines to destroy the Jiaoji Railway to prevent their eastward movement. (8) The Japanese office was located in the Japanese dormitory of the Gongda Yarn Factory, and the Chinese office was located on the third floor of the Hongtai Market in Beiping and the third floor of the market in Taitong Town. Items nine, ten, and eleven are unknown. After obtaining the confessions, the Public Security Bureau immediately ordered a temporary martial law to be implemented. Starting at 6:00 PM that night, double guards were added, and starting at 10:00 PM, all pedestrians were strictly interrogated. Security teams and patrol officers from various branch bureaus were dispatched in shifts to patrol in order to ensure thoroughness. At the same time, they requested the Navy to transfer all the Marine Corps stationed in Chengyang back to Qingdao to cooperate in defense. The traitors knew that the matter had been exposed, and because the military and police were already prepared, they dared not act that night. On the 25th, the Public Security Bureau ordered the arrested traitors Sun Zuochen and others to act as informants and arrested more than 20 traitors in Sifang and Cangkou. The remaining unarrested traitors had already fled upon hearing the news. The Public Security Bureau is currently searching for them. (27th)

Situation of the Kailuan Labor Strike 106

Japanese Instructors Helped Workers Establish Two Organizations

Workers Paraded and Demonstrated, Demanding Compensation

Workers at the East Fourth Mine Decided Not to Participate in the Strike

Tianjin Correspondence: The Kailuan Tangshan mine strike, which began on the 18th, has been going on for ten days. Although the strike has not spread, it will take some time to resolve. Tao Shangming returned to Tangshan on the 22nd to cooperate with Gu Zhen, the assistant manager of Kailuan Mines, and Xu Huidong, the director of the Civil Affairs Department of the Hebei Provincial Party Headquarters, to mediate between labor and management. The striking workers demanded police compensation and coal bonuses from the mine, as well as an increase in wages of eight points and the issuance of monthly coal tickets to each person. On the other hand, they demanded compensation for the wounded and dead from the Public Security Bureau. The mine has not yet responded to the conditions proposed by the workers. The workers established two organizations on the 23rd: (1) the Hebei Province War Zone Mine Workers Autonomous Joint General Union and (2) the Labor-Management Cooperation General Society. A congress was held at the Tianhe Inn at the station on the same day, with the participation of a dispatch team from the Japanese Tangshan Military Police, which seemed to be guiding them. After the establishment of the two organizations, offices were set up on Guangdong Street, and Zhao Dazhong was elected as the chairman by the workers. Zhao was previously a low-ranking officer in the puppet army. He came to Luan County last year and, relying on the power of the Japanese, became involved with some workers. Zhao Xun, the director of the Public Security Bureau, fearing that the striking workers would be exploited by foreigners, summoned the representatives to discuss the matter. The workers initially proposed eighteen demands, then twelve. The important conditions were to provide generous compensation for the wounded and dead, to punish the perpetrators who opened fire, and to guarantee that such incidents would not occur again in the future. Although the authorities knew that their demands were excessive, they feared that excessive rejection would easily lead to the expansion of the strike, so they agreed to continue the discussion. On the 23rd, the striking workers learned that the workers from the East Fourth Mine (Majiagou, Zhaogezhuang, Gucheng, Linxi) had issued a declaration that they would not provide any assistance to the Tangshan mine strike, so some workers became quite repentant. Many of the inner shift workers were persuaded by the mine manager and the engineers to start working. However, many more workers were coerced by the striking workers and did not immediately return to work. Although the striking workers insisted that they would not stop until they achieved their goals, they actually had few supporters, and their arrogance had also diminished. Only three or four hundred people with certain backgrounds refused to stop and had even organized a workers' joint team, divided into four large teams and three platoons, with leaders and other titles. Each worker wore a red cloth strip and carried a wooden stick, parading through the city like a military force. On the 24th, because the inner shift workers resumed work, the striking workers gathered outside the mine entrance and prevented food from being sent in, causing the inner shift workers to go without food and were forced to stop working. On the same day, the workers presented a demand to Tao Shangming that whether from the government or the mine, funds must be provided to compensate the wounded and dead workers, 2,000 yuan for each death and 500 yuan for each injured person. Tao Shangming refused to accept this, and the workers threatened to hold a large-scale parade and demonstration. Tao, fearing an accident, tried his best to stop them and summoned Zhao Dazhong, the chairman elected by the workers, for face-to-face negotiations. Tao agreed to convey the workers' demands to the mine and provide generous compensation for the wounded and dead. The workers had nothing more to say at this point, but they demanded a quick reply, otherwise, they would still parade and demonstrate. The workers of the Dongsi mine, because the actions of the Tang mine workers exceeded the norm, issued two declarations: one, advising the workers of the Dongsi mine not to be incited by others to join the Tang mine strike, and two, advising the Tang mine workers to repent as soon as possible and not to be traitors for others to exploit. The Tang mine striking workers, seeing that the Dongsi mine expressed unexpected intentions, also issued declarations and posted slogans with the words "Down with the Dongsi mine workers union." The mine and the authorities are now optimistic about the matter, that is, the Dongsi mine will not be affected by the Tang mine strike, and that the Tang mine strike is only a small number of people's activities, which is not worth worrying about. However, the gunpowder depot of the Tangshan Qixin Cement Plant suddenly exploded yesterday morning, and all the gunpowder was destroyed. A bomb was also found in front of the Xinyu Gong on Xiaoma Road, which inevitably made people feel uneasy, and the background became more obvious. The Tangshan Public Security Bureau then announced martial law again, and the gates in the city were closed tightly from 8:00 PM to 6:00 AM the next morning. (15th)

Songjiang: Disputes Over District Establishment After Division 107

Previously, the county received instructions from the Department of Civil Affairs that, for the convenience of promoting autonomy, it had previously held a district division meeting and decided to divide the sixteen districts into eight districts. Regarding the location of the district offices, a follow-up meeting was held today (28th) to summon the original townships and towns to merge as much as possible according to the standards promulgated by the department, with a standard of 500 to 1,000 households. After a decision is made, it will be submitted to the province for approval. However, each district has many disputes over the location of the district office. For example, when Zhangze and Yexie are merged, it was originally decided to set up a district branch office in Yexie. When Xiaokunshan and Tianmashan are merged, the district office will be set up in Xiaokunshan. When Xinzhuangzhuang and Qibao are merged, the district office will be set up in Wujiatang. When Shanyang and Caoging are merged, the district office will be set up in Caoging. However, at today's meeting, the people of Zhangze, Tianmashan, Xinzhuang, and Shanyang had many disputes over the location of the district, and the debate was fierce and could not be resolved. After voting, it was decided to submit it to the province for approval after the county government investigates.

Wuxi: Expansion of the Li Shuyun Case 108

Liu Zhuomin, the former director of the Second Public Security Bureau, refused to hand over [his duties], involving the case of Li Shuyun, the wife of Director Gu of the Department of Civil Affairs. The county court telegraphed Gu to appear in court for questioning. Li Shuyun has also hired lawyer Chao Kun to sue Gu Renfa for bigamy, and the case is expanding. The details are listed below: (1) The county court prosecutor's office telegraphed the province to request Gu Renfa to appear in court for questioning. The province replied by telegram that Gu had gone from Jiangxi to Wuhan and could not appear in court. Now that Gu has returned to the province and is working as usual, and the case was reported by Director Gu of the Department of Civil Affairs, it is necessary to appear in court for questioning. Therefore, another telegram has been sent to the province requesting Gu to bring evidence to Wuxi to testify, so that the case can be easily investigated. (2) The prosecutor's office continued to sign and summon Liu Zhuomin for questioning in court yesterday afternoon. Liu confessed that he owed 400 yuan in public funds due to handover matters, so he went to Zhenjiang to borrow money. He did not expect Wuxi to be eager to take over, so his wife sent a quick letter urging him to return and handle the handover. This proves that there was no resistance. As for the letters sent by friends in Jiangxi, they were ordinary socializing and had no other effect. After questioning, he was sent back to prison. (3) After 5:00 PM the day before yesterday, Chief Qian continued to summon Li Shuyun to inquire in detail about the marriage issue with Director Gu. Li confessed that she was indeed Gu's legal wife and only learned this year that Gu still had a wife. She then asked him for a solution, but Gu was summoned to Jiangxi and promised to make a satisfactory solution after returning to the province. Unexpectedly, Director Gu of the Department of Civil Affairs reported her for selling official positions and accumulating money, fearing that she would accuse him of bigamy or fraud marriage, so he took this preemptive measure. After questioning, she was still sent back to prison. (4) The initiation of this case stemmed from Liu Zhuomin's refusal to hand over [his duties]. Liu's wife, Wen Rongzhen, also claimed to be surnamed Li and to be sisters with Li Shuyun. Now that they are in the same cell, they rarely talk after meeting. Shuyun blamed her for not climbing the social ladder and falsely claiming relatives, which has caused her mother and daughter to be imprisoned. She asked, "Can you be at peace with your conscience?" Wen was blamed and speechless, but behind Li's back, she said, "He came to complain to me. The fact is that Director Gu wanted to divorce him, so he made a trap and used my husband as a starting point. Now we are harmed by him." The truth in this is worth pondering. (5) When Li Shuyun and her daughter were arrested in Shanghai, they hired three lawyers, Zhang Shizhao, Xiang Xun, and Tan Xinzhen, to defend them. After they were transferred to Wuxi, they transferred the case to lawyer Chao Kun to handle. Yesterday, lawyer Chao came to Wuxi from Shanghai and visited Li Shuyun in the detention center. Li happened to be taken out of the women's prison to wait for questioning. Li said that she went to Shanghai from Zhenjiang on the 17th for medical treatment and lived with her mother in Huang Gongguan. She sent a quick letter to Gu, and the receipt for the quick letter is with Mr. Huang (a European). There is other evidence in Huang's house that can be obtained. She immediately wrote a letter saying, "Please give all the evidence to lawyer Chao. To Mr. Huang, Gu Li Shuyun." She also expressed gnashing hatred for the case, saying, "I have decided to countersue for bigamy and fraud marriage. I have been harmed to such an extent. Why not countersue?" Li's face was thin, her spirit was sluggish, she groaned constantly, and her illness had not yet healed. Those who saw her could not help but feel compassion. (6) Lawyer Chao told reporters that the case was initially divided into two parts: (A) Li Shuyun flaunted and sold official positions, (B) Instigated Liu Zhuomin and his wife to obstruct official duties. Li Shuyun is in the position of the defendant. The prosecutor's office is investigating the case. Now Li firmly insists on suing Gu for bigamy and fraud marriage. Li is in the position of the plaintiff. Whether Gu has committed bigamy should be investigated by the prosecutor's office after the lawsuit is filed. As for the wife of the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs being arrested in a case, the district chief of the subordinate Water Police District was ordered to arrest her in person. If the wife of the Minister of the Navy needed to be summoned for something, would the Marine Corps be ordered to arrest her? This can be said to be a ridiculous story. (7) Yesterday, news was received from the capital that the Li Shuyun case is involving more and more people. Gu's wife, Ai Chengmei, who now lives in Nanjing, has sued Gu for bigamy in the capital's court. (8) Yan Shenyu, the county magistrate of this county, immediately telegraphed the province to resign after the case occurred. Various local groups telegraphed to retain him. Yan continued to request resignation again. Chairman Chen of the provincial government, considering the public's strong desire to retain him, appointed Zeng Binqiu, the director of the Second Section of the Department of Civil Affairs, who was inspecting Changshu, and made a long-distance call to ask him to go to Wuxi to console and retain him. After Zeng arrived in Wuxi, he met with County Magistrate Yan and explained the province's expectations. However, Yan's determination to leave was very strong. Because Director Gu had returned to the department to handle affairs, he would go to Zhenjiang on the 27th to present everything to Chairman Chen and Director Gu in person. It is now heard that after the sincere consolation of the provincial department, he has dispelled the intention to resign. (9) Zeng Binqiu, the director of the Second Section of the Department of Civil Affairs, was appointed to Wuxi and stayed at the New World Hotel under the pseudonym Hu Zhengong. His whereabouts were extremely confidential. He first went to the residence of Li Wengong, the director of the Public Security Bureau, to discuss something. He stayed at Li's residence that night, and only met with County Magistrate Yan the next day.

Qingdao Mayor Visits Wuxi 109

Shen Honglie, the mayor of Qingdao, accompanied by Gao Lingbai, the secretary of the National Government, arrived in Zhenjiang from Beijing the day before yesterday to visit important industrial, commercial, and educational institutions. At 10:00 AM yesterday, they went from Zhenjiang to the Qishuyan Power Plant to visit. At 2:40 PM, they arrived in Wuxi and stayed at the Yangxin New World Hotel. Because he was in Shanxi, Secretary Ye represented him and accompanied Yang Hanxi, the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, to the station to greet them. Yang Weizhang, the son of Mr. Yang and the current president of the Industrial Bank, accompanied them on detailed visits to the Lixin Textile Bleaching and Finishing Factory, Qingfeng and Guangqin Textile Factories, Gansheng Silk Factory, and the Provincial People's Education Institute. The Chamber of Commerce hosted a banquet that night to welcome them. Today (29th), they will continue to visit.

Zhenjiang: New Jiangsu Province Regulations for Opium Suppression 110

In order to eliminate opium addiction within a time limit, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has specially formulated organizational regulations for the Opium Suppression Committee, investigation methods for registering addicts, and methods for distributing the use of fines. After several discussions at the provincial government meeting, a general decision has been made and submitted to Chairman Chiang for review. As soon as it is approved, it will be implemented. It is heard that the organizational regulations stipulate that a Provincial Opium Suppression Committee shall be established at the provincial level and a County Opium Suppression Committee shall be established at the county level, organized by the provincial and county agencies together with local impartial gentry. Separate methods for mandatory abstinence within a time limit will be formulated for party, government, military, police, public officials, and students. Special attention will be paid to the land producing opium seedlings in the Xuhai area. Addicts will be ordered to register and obtain licenses within a time limit. Those who fail to do so will not be issued licenses. All license fees and fines from private addicts will be used for health undertakings, opium suppression propaganda, police team inspection fees, rural relief, and special construction costs.

Nantong: Merging All County Public Security Bureaus 111

All eighteen public security bureaus in the county will be merged into nine bureaus starting next month. The county government will also select the directors of the branch bureaus: Shen Denghai for the urban area, Jin Ding for Tangzha, Wang Xiguang for the port area, Chen Renzi for Liuqiao, Li Youguang for Shigang, Deng Hancheng for Jinsha, Gu Minyu for Jinghua, Xu Ruxiang for Yudong, and Chen Qicai for Liuhai Sha.

Huzhou: New Ling Steamer Robbed in Broad Daylight 112

The express boat from Linghu to Xinshi was robbed on the morning of the 25th of this month. When it passed Xiaonei River, about four miles from Qianjin, a bandit boat suddenly appeared. Four bandits, two of whom were holding wooden cases, ordered the express boat to stop. The boat owner, Ma Yuhua, saw that the bandits had guns and dared not resist, so he ordered the boat crew to moor the boat. The bandits boarded the boat and searched at will, robbing the boat owner Ma Yuhua of 25 yuan in silver dollars, over 100 small silver coins, Qianji goods worth 50 yuan in silver dollars, Zhengchang goods worth 100 yuan in silver dollars, Yongda worth 2.3 yuan, and over 10 yuan from each of the passengers. The bandits then sped away in the original boat. Afterwards, the boat owner, Ma Yuhua, sailed the boat back and reported the robbery to the Qianjin Water Police Team before reporting the robbery to the various agencies in Linghu and requesting them to pursue and arrest the bandits.

Special Article

Public Discussion of Enrichment (Continued) by Zhang Yuanruo 113

(4) National Economy (Note 12)

(1) The law of enrichment is a response to social life. The spirit of constitutionalism should evolve with the times and be reformed due to changes in social life. In the past, people were oppressed by monarchs and aristocrats, so political freedom was the only good remedy for liberating the people and the most important and precious principle when drafting a constitution. Today's society has changed its old appearance. The suffering of the people from the oppression of capital is far greater than the political oppression of the past, so economic liberation is the urgent requirement of the people of today. Therefore, the purpose of modern constitutionalism is not only to seek the protection of political rights, but also to attach importance to the protection of economic rights; not only to ensure the freedom of the people, but also to impose necessary social obligations on the people. However, the law is not a subjective formality. The essential condition for its implementation is objective fact. An empty law is not enough to implement itself, and a painted cake is not enough to satisfy hunger. This is the main reason for the failure of constitutionalism in China since the Republic, and a factual problem that those who care about the rule of law should earnestly study in the future. After the European War, the world's constitutions have undergone a great change, all with a spirit of socialism. "However, this kind of movement was initially just blind following, and few were able to consider it calmly. Therefore, in the end, political power still belonged to the moderates. This victory of moderation is actually a major fact in the post-war revolutionary movement and the new constitutions of various countries." (Note 13) Therefore, after the war, countries such as Yugoslavia, Romania, Estonia, Lithuania, and Poland were extremely left-leaning at first, but due to the influence of the German Revolution, they all changed their minds. Even the stubborn Soviet Russia eventually changed its course due to practical political experience and the control of objective conditions.

China is plagued by many disasters. The people are deeply devastated by natural and man-made disasters, and oppressed by foreign aggression and internal turmoil. The industry is declining, and the production technology is immature, resulting in the general public not being able to maintain their minimum standard of living. Those who are trapped by hunger and cold and wandering in the gutters are too numerous to count. Therefore, the urgent task for China today is to jointly seek to recuperate and develop national capital. Reckless destruction is not tolerated by socio-economic conditions. Even completely imitating the moderate German constitution is sometimes not allowed by objective facts. The constitution is not something that is written behind closed doors but something that grows. The provisions of the constitution must be based on the foundation of society to have the possibility of actual implementation. Therefore, today's drafters or critics of the constitution should have a down-to-earth and pragmatic spirit. Otherwise, the magnificent constitution will not only be useless, but will also be mutually incompatible and run counter to the social foundation and economic situation.

Based on this principle, although we are not entirely satisfied with Chapter 3 of the draft constitution in theory, we dare not go too high in practice and make emotional criticisms. The reason why political opinions have been complicated and ineffective in the past is precisely due to this drawback. If the government can truly seek to implement each and every provision of the constitution, it is already commendable. Moreover, since our country's industry is immature, if individual enterprises can seek to avoid harming the interests of the country and the nation, it is also necessary to encourage their development. We should not completely obliterate them because of longing for the realm of extreme socialism. (Note 14)

What we are dissatisfied with is roughly two points. (1) Developing national capital is extremely important, but the constitution does not have a single provision for this, which seems regrettable. Article 156 of the German Constitution can be used as a reference, but it does not need to be completely copied. (2) Article 31 of the draft constitution advocates labor-capital coordination. In principle, there is nothing to criticize, and it is very in line with national conditions. However, how this principle should be implemented is not found in the entire constitution, which is equivalent to empty talk. Here, Chapter 5, Article 165 of the German Constitution can be used as a reference. At the same time, Italy's political system and trade union system can also be used as a reference. (Note 15) (To be continued)

Local News

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Cables Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Revise Sino-American Commercial Treaty 114

Repeal Ban on Chinese Entering America

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce yesterday cabled the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in Nanjing, "According to your esteemed office, the Sino-American Commercial Treaty of the 29th year of Guangxu, which is now due to expire and be revised, does not stipulate how Chinese people residing in the United States should be treated. The stipulations only restrict continued travel by Chinese laborers and do not apply to officials, educators, students, merchants, and tourists. This is actually the Chinese Labor Treaty of the 20th year of Guangxu. This time, regarding the ban on Chinese laborers, whether to revise it together is something the Chamber cannot determine. However, according to Article 1 of the treaty, the United States' self-imposed restrictions on Chinese laborers returning to the United States must not contradict the provisions of this treaty. Therefore, the United States' self-imposed regulations, which add restrictions outside the text of the treaty, originally violate the treaty. Moreover, self-imposed regulations refer to Chinese laborers returning to the United States, while merchants, students, and five other categories of people originally have the wording 'enjoying the benefits of residing in the United States without hindrance.' Therefore, the United States has no right to self-impose regulations to restrict these five categories of people, which is perfectly clear. The United States Immigration Bureau distorts the meaning of 'merchant' to refer to international trade and restricts teachers, only allowing university professors to enter the United States while rejecting primary and secondary school teachers. This is clearly creating new problems outside the treaty. Therefore, what is being contested today is not the issue of signing or revising the treaty, but the issue of the execution of the treaty. The origin of this problem lies in the fact that past envoys and consuls have allowed the Immigration Bureau to act recklessly and have not argued based on the treaty, resulting in Chinese people encountering obstacles when entering the United States. If the Chinese Labor Treaty of the 20th year of Guangxu can be revised during this treaty revision, it would be very good. Otherwise, the meaning of merchants and students should be clearly defined in the continued Commercial Treaty to avoid arbitrary obstruction by customs officials in that country. This is a unanimous demand of the entire country. We respectfully request your esteemed ministry to review and implement it for the sake of public convenience. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce bows respectfully, Qin."

New Life Movement to be Held in Shanghai on April 1 121

According to the Central News Agency, since Chairman Chiang Kai-shek launched the New Life Movement in Nanchang, the whole country has responded and it has become a temporary trend. The Central Mass Movement Guidance Committee has also issued a telegram calling on the masses to work hard to promote it. The precariousness of our country's national strength and the desolation of people's lives cannot be revived without hard work. The way of revolution must be concise and ensure that the general public has national morality and knowledge, so that society can progress. Therefore, enduring hardship and hard work, practicing thrift, reforming bad habits, and abstaining from extravagance to cultivate clean and simple habits are the basic work for saving the country and preserving its existence. Since the establishment of the preparatory office of the New Life Movement Promotion Association in Shanghai, various circles have joined one after another, and the number of initiators has reached more than 500. Mayor Wu Tiecheng, in order to urge the progress, convened a meeting yesterday afternoon, and leading figures from the party, government, and military circles, including Tao Baichuan, Pan Gongzhan, Wu Kaixian, Jiang Huaisu, Yu Hongjun, etc., attended the meeting to discuss the guiding principles, propaganda outlines, and organizational regulations of the New Life Movement.
