The promotion work is divided into several phases. Mayor Wu believes that order and cleanliness are the first practical goal. Therefore, he has instructed the Public Security Bureau and the Health Bureau to formulate implementation methods and instructed the police to give guidance and work with the people to implement it.

Aviation Administration to Build Two Airplanes 124

"Batavia Overseas Chinese" and "Air Force Comrade"

To be Named Upon Completion

According to the Aviation Association, overseas Chinese in Batavia, in order to promote aviation to save the country and develop the motherland's aviation industry, previously raised a large sum of money and remitted it to the Aviation Administration in China to build the "Batavia Overseas Chinese" aircraft. The "Air Force Comrade" aircraft, donated by all officers and soldiers of the Aviation Administration, was also built independently by the factory. Song Ziwen to Go to Northwest This Week 126

Met with Reporters Yesterday to Report on Mission of Trip

Date of Inspection of Shaanxi and Gansu Provinces Set for One Month

Song Ziwen, Standing Committee Member of the National Economic Council, returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday after attending the plenary session of the council in Beijing. Mr. Song is scheduled to depart for the Northwest this week for an inspection. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Mr. Song met with a group of reporters at the council's Shanghai office and announced the mission of this inspection trip. A summary of his remarks is recorded as follows:

Departing This Week 127

Mr. Song first stated that, regarding the Northwest inspection, it was originally scheduled to depart on the 28th (yesterday) with Dai Jitao, President of the Examination Yuan, etc. However, because some procedures have not yet been prepared, the departure date has been slightly postponed. President Dai has already departed from Beijing today (yesterday) with several foreign experts, while he himself has decided to depart from Shanghai within a week. However, the report that he is scheduled to travel by Eurasian plane on the 3rd of next month is not true. This trip is scheduled to last for one month, and only Cai Shousun, Chen Zhixiang, and Qin Yingchun, the council's secretaries, will accompany him.

Scope of Inspection 128

Mr. Song continued, "The itinerary for this trip is to first go to Xi'an in Shaanxi to meet with President Dai, then to Lanzhou in Gansu. Whether to go to Qinghai will depend on the time available and will be decided at that time. Due to various reasons, it is not convenient to go to Xinjiang at this time. As for the trip to Sichuan, it will be made after returning to Shanghai. As for the scope of the inspection, it will focus on roads, water conservancy, and sanitation. Furthermore, the council's Northwest Office has already been established in Xi'an, and Liu Jinshan has been appointed as the director. There are some issues at the office that still need to be discussed with me in person."

Allocation Method 129

Regarding the future work of the National Economic Council, Mr. Song answered a reporter's question and said that the National Economic Council's funding has always been diverted from the US cotton and wheat loans. The amount of this loan has been reduced to 20 million US dollars, which is approximately 50 million yuan in national currency. After deducting the principal repayment and transportation costs, only 12.3 million yuan can be used. The conference passed a resolution to use this amount, with 16 million yuan used to reorganize the currency system, and 15 million yuan used for the National Economic Council's construction expenses this year. The allocation has also been decided as follows: 6,800,000 yuan for roads, 500,000 yuan for sanitation, 1,000,000 yuan for the cotton industry, 750,000 yuan for the silk industry, 1,900,000 yuan for Jiangxi construction, 2,500,000 yuan for Northwest construction, 64,000 yuan for the tea industry, 100,000 yuan for fuel research, 200,000 yuan for economic research, 750,000 yuan for general management fees and expert expenses, and 436,000 yuan for reserve funds, totaling 15,000,000 yuan.

Rajchman to Leave China 130

As for the League of Nations' technical cooperation with China, Rajchman, the expert sent to China, has indeed decided to leave China in the near future. Because the League of Nations Executive Council meeting is scheduled to be held in Geneva on May 16, the League of Nations General Assembly has specially summoned Rajchman back to report on his work in China in order to understand the situation and be prepared to report at the meeting on time. The rumors that Rajchman is resigning this time are not true.

The incident of British troops invading and occupying Ban Hong is serious and has attracted the attention of people across the country. More than a dozen people attended, including Zhang Yaozeng, Lü Tianmin, Sun Ji'an, Yang Jialin, and Zhao Zhi. The meeting was chaired by Zhang Yaozeng, the executive director. Alarming news has spread, shocking us. Ban Hong is located in southwestern Yunnan, covering thousands of square miles and is rich in gold, silver, and coal mines. It has always been part of our country's territory. This time, the British took advantage of our country's difficulties and used the same old trick of occupying Pianma by force, seizing it by force and treating China as nothing. All those with blood and courage cannot but be furious. The only way forward is to urge the government to negotiate seriously with the United Kingdom to ensure that British troops withdraw as soon as possible and persevere until the goal is achieved. The fundamental plan is that the government and the people must cooperate sincerely, determine borders, rectify internal affairs, develop transportation, consolidate border defense, develop mineral resources, and revitalize industry to make our country strong and prosperous and prevent others from coveting it. We are patriotic and dare not lag behind. We vow to follow people from all walks of life to act as a diplomatic support. We respectfully announce this to you for your consideration. Tiannan Society, Great China University, Shanghai, bows respectfully."

Industrial and Commercial Circles Request Correction of Trademark Law Interpretation 132

Only Discussing Shape, Not Sound, Easily Leads to Counterfeiting

Qian Chengxu Entered Beijing Last Night to Discuss with the Ministry of Industry

According to the Riri News Agency, after the Judicial Yuan announced its interpretation of the Trademark Law, Hu Xiyuan and other members of the Shanghai Industrial Federation believed that it only discussed shape and not sound, which would easily lead to counterfeiting and would invalidate the protection of trademarks. They sent a joint letter to the Industrial Federation, appointing Qian Chengxu to enter Beijing last night by night express to request the Ministry of Industry to correct it and provide another interpretation. The details are recorded below:

Letter Requesting Correction 133

Hu Xiyuan and other members of the China Industrial Federation sent a joint letter to the Industrial Federation yesterday, stating: "We are writing to you to express our shock at the news that the Judicial Yuan's interpretation of Article 1, Paragraph 2 of the Trademark Law only discusses shape and not sound. Although our country has a vast territory and complex dialects, this has not been the case since today. However, the pronunciation of characters has always been based on the national pronunciation as the standard, so it is not without a standard. Now, abandoning sound and only paying attention to shape will inevitably lead to increased disputes over butterflies and nonsense. The hard-earned industrial and commercial enterprises will lose their protection. We believe that this is unacceptable. We plan to ask your association to state the advantages and disadvantages and request the Ministry of Industry to correct it quickly. Is this appropriate? We hope for your wise decision."

Qian Chengxu's Trip to Beijing 134

Qian Chengxu, the executive director of the China Industrial Federation, due to the joint request of the members, took the express train to Beijing last night to discuss the matter with the industry authorities. According to Qian's remarks before his departure, "The education of the Chinese people is not yet widespread. Most people in the interior recognize the sound of goods and are careless about recognizing the characters. Now, the Judicial Yuan's interpretation that the same sound does not entail responsibility is tantamount to fundamentally invalidating the protection of trademarks. For example, the trademark of Shenxin brand cotton yarn is a 'Ren Zhong' (person bell). Not long ago, several factories renamed Japanese yarn as 'Chen Zhong' (morning bell) and sold it as Shenxin's Ren Zhong brand. This matter later caused a very big problem. I think society can still remember this matter. Cases like this, the law cannot be too strict, but in view of the facts, the Chinese situation is like this, we should guard against it before it happens. Otherwise, disputes in the future will inevitably arise one after another, and both merchants and factories will be affected. This can be asserted. This time I am entering the capital at the joint request of many members of the China Industrial Association to discuss countermeasures with the central industry authorities to seek remedies. It is expected that the Ministry of Industry will ask the Ministry of Justice to provide another interpretation to achieve the goal."

Jiangnan Railway Company Approved to Build Railway Through Five Provinces 139

Wuhu-Sunjiafu Section to Open to Traffic by the End of Next Month

Central News Agency reports that the Jiangnan Railway Company has always held grand aspirations for the construction of transportation projects. The Wuhu-Zha Railway's Wuhu-Sunjiafu section (Wuhu to Sunjiafu), recently built by the company, is scheduled to hold a traffic opening ceremony by the end of next month. Furthermore, according to reliable sources, the company, in order to develop transportation in the five southeastern provinces, resolved at the last shareholders' meeting to build the Beijing-Wuhu Railway. Recently, shareholders Zhang Jingjiang, et al., obtained approval from the Ministry of Railways to plan the construction of the five-province railway from Beijing to the border of Fujian and Guangdong. Moreover, for the sake of business and transportation prospects, they decided to hold a shareholders' meeting on April 12 to discuss everything. Details are as follows:

Wuhu-Sunjiafu Section to Open to Traffic by the End of Next Month 140

The Wuhu-Sunjiafu Railway, built by the company, is being constructed on the original Wuhu-Guangde Railway line. Since its commencement, the section between Wuhu and Wangzhi has been completed. All sections from Wangzhi to Sunjiafu in Xuancheng have also been completed in sequence. It is now decided to hold the traffic opening ceremony by the end of next month.

Five-Province Railway Approved for Construction 141

Shareholders of the company, such as Zhang Jingjiang, et al., recognizing that transportation in the five southeastern provinces is not yet fully convenient, obtained approval from the Ministry of Railways to plan the construction of the five-province railway from the capital to the border of Fujian and Guangdong, passing through the five provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Fujian, and Guangdong, with a total length of more than one thousand kilometers. Using the most economical method, it will require at least 30 million yuan. It is now decided to proceed in five stages. The Beijing-Wuhu section has already begun construction, with a total length of more than eighty kilometers, costing about two million. It is planned to be completed by the end of this year, or at the latest by February of next spring, in order to connect with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway. The second section is the Wuhu-Sunjiafu section currently under construction. The remaining three sections, from Sunjiafu in Xuancheng to Jiangshan in Zhejiang, from Jiangshan to Yanping in Fujian, and from Yanping to Zhao'an in Guangdong, are now beginning surveying. Once the surveying is completed, construction will be undertaken sequentially.

Regular Shareholders' Meeting Scheduled 142

Furthermore, for the sake of business and transportation prospects, the company will hold a shareholders' meeting on April 12 at its office at 393 Ferguson Road to decide on all matters in progress.

Qiantang River Railway Bridge to Be Built, Railway Bureau Proceeding to Complete Shanghai-Ningbo Line 143

First, Purchase of Land from Cao'e River to Xixing

Advancing Construction of the Bridge 144

The stipulated budget for the construction of the Qiantang River Railway Bridge is five million yuan. A two million yuan loan was obtained from five banks, including Shanghai Zhejiang Xingye Bank, scheduled to be resolved in installments by the end of June of this year, with an annual interest rate of one percent, to be paid off in six years. A loan of 160,000 pounds was obtained from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Administration Committee, and a loan of one million yuan was obtained from the National Economic Council. The Zhejiang Provincial Government has hired Zhang Renjie, Gu Mengyu, Ye Zhuotang, and others as committee members to plan and proceed in order to complete the project as soon as possible.

Purchasing Civilian Land 145

This section is estimated to cost more than 5.6 million yuan: 31 kilometers from the Cao'e River to Shaoxing, and 47 kilometers from Shaoxing to Xixing. Now that the route has already been designated, it has been decided to first purchase civilian land in the section from the Cao'e River to Xixing and then begin construction.

After Completion 146

The population density in the Shaoxing area is the same as that in the Ningbo section. In terms of cargo, the products include vegetable oil, tin foil, Shaoxing wine, fresh fruit, grain cocoons, cotton, cotton yarn, sugar cane, lime, coarse paper, north-south foods, salted fish, and tobacco. It is found that the Ningbo section carries approximately 130,000 tons of cargo annually, of which 30 percent goes to and from Shaoxing, and 40 percent goes to and from Xixing, transshipped to Zhuji, Lanxi, and other places. Calculated at the average third-class freight rate, the annual income is approximately 250,000 yuan, which, together with passenger transport, is at least 600,000 yuan. In the future, after completion, the revenue of the Railway Bureau will certainly increase.

International Trade Bureau Handling Jiangxi Tea Exchange for Polish Goods 147

He Bingxian Currently in Contact with the Polish Embassy

Industrialists Express That the Future is Difficult

Guowen News Agency reports that the local International Trade Bureau, previously ordered by the Ministry of Industry to find a way to sell Jiangxi's abundant Wuning tea abroad, would exchange 1 million yuan worth of Ning tea for the same value of kerosene from the Soviet Union to avoid either side feeling exploited. Consequently, He Bingxian, the director of the bureau, took responsibility for contacting the Russian side. However, it is recently rumored that the exchange of Jiangxi tea for Russian oil is no longer possible, and there is another proposal to exchange for goods of the same value from Poland. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, the reporter inquired with He Bingxian, the director of the International Trade Bureau, and industrialists about the details. The information obtained is as follows:

Exchange for Russian Oil Failed 148

According to Mr. He, the reporter first learned that the bureau was ordered by the Ministry of Industry to handle the exchange of Ning tea for oil from the Soviet Union. At that time, he contacted the Soviet Union's Youbiandi Company, which operates oil in China. Unexpectedly, after consultation between the two parties, the Soviet Union's gasoline coal sold to China had to be purchased with cash due to accounting reasons, while the shipment of Chinese tea to Russia would only be paid for after one year. Because of this problem, Chinese tea is already in decline, and there is no centralized purchasing agency for this million yuan of Jiangxi tea. If small-scale operators have to wait a year to get the price, their finances will of course be unable to circulate, and they will be unable to continue. Therefore, it was terminated.

Poland Agreed to Exchange Goods 149

As for exchanging goods with Poland, it is true. However, it is still under study. The matter came about because the Polish ambassador mentioned it to Minister Chen when he passed through Nanjing from the north a few days ago. He said that China has 4 million of Jiangxi Ning tea, and in order to promote Sino-Polish trade, it can be sold to Poland, but the price of 4 million yuan must be used to purchase goods in Poland for shipment to China. Therefore, he is considering proceeding with the matter with the counselor of the Polish embassy, and it is expected to be decided soon.

Industrialists Express Difficulties 150

Subsequently, the reporter inquired with industrialists about the possibility of Sino-Polish exchange of goods. They learned that there are many difficulties in exchanging Polish goods for Chinese tea. According to customs import and export tables over the years, Polish goods sold to China are very small, while goods shipped from China to Poland are even fewer. Most of the Polish goods shipped to China are cotton and silk textiles, while those shipped from China to Poland are dried shrimp, pork intestines, black tea, peanuts, nets, and untanned hides. Although the total number of Polish shipments to China in 1928 reached more than 2,587,000 yuan, 2.5 million yuan of which were military supplies. Therefore, according to these statistics, it is actually impossible. Even if it can be exchanged, the goods that China wants to exchange for, no matter what the value, still need to be carefully studied.

A Glimpse of Sino-Polish Trade 151

The following is a record of customs reports on Sino-Polish trade over the years, counted from 1864 to 1932. Only from 1924 (i.e., the 13th year of the Republic of China) was there a definite record. The numbers are as follows:

Navigation Conference Resolves to Establish Maritime Court 152

First in Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, and Guangdong

Attached to Local Courts

The shipping industries of various countries are developed and well-organized. When major ship disputes occur, they are handled by maritime courts. China does not yet have such a judicial organ for handling ships. In recent years, although the Navigation Bureaus of Shanghai, Hankou, Tianjin, and Guangdong have established ship collision arbitration committees, they are still limited to collision matters. When major accidents occur on ships, there is still no legal organ to handle them. This has led to the shelving of major tragic cases over the years. For example, the Xin Kang ship was sunk by a Japanese ship, resulting in hundreds of deaths. The Tu Nan ship was sunk by the Chang Chun Wan, also drowning more than a hundred passengers and crew members. The perpetrators are not held responsible, the victims have no way to redress their grievances, and those who suffer losses often suffer losses. This has long-term consequences and is a matter of great concern. The organization of a maritime court cannot be delayed any longer. Among the agenda items discussed at this navigation conference, the most important, in addition to the recovery of inland waterway rights and the determination of navigation funds, is the organization of a maritime court, which is the most urgent. The conference proposed and agreed on a method of organizing one maritime court each in the important commercial ports of Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, Guangzhou, Qingdao, and other places. The maritime court will be attached to the local court. The position of president of the court will be filled by the appointment of a navigation expert with legal knowledge who has served as a shipowner for more than five years. As for the positions of judge and clerk, they will also be selected from legal scholars who are well-versed in navigation. The detailed organizational rules will be jointly determined by the Ministry of Transportation and the Ministry of Judicial Administration. Because this case is urgent to implement, it has been resolved by the conference and submitted to the Ministry for prompt action. It has been decided to first organize and establish it in Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, and Guangdong.

Merger of Wired and Wireless Telegraph Agencies May Be Realized 159

Telecom Circles Express Approval and Are Studying Implementation

No Agreement Yet on Joint Establishment of Postal and Telegraph Branches

In order to innovate telecommunications administration, the Ministry of Transportation plans to merge wired and wireless telegraph bureaus and stations, instructing each bureau and station to study and contribute opinions. Yesterday, the reporter interviewed the heads of the local telecommunications administration to inquire about their views on this. According to the answer, wired and wireless are both national operating agencies, and they naturally strongly agree with the principle of merging. They also talked about the improvement of wired telegraph in recent years and the merger of postal branches and telegraph offices in this city. Details are as follows:

Line Consolidation: Wired telegraph has been established since the late Qing Dynasty and has been around for decades. Although there are regulations for minor repairs every three years and major repairs every five years, they were only nominally enforced due to the unstable political situation. Those handling telecommunications administration also regarded it as a government office, resulting in corruption and delays, and the industry was not thriving. Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, the Ministry of Transportation has actively reorganized it in recent years. Last year, a total of 5,371 kilometers of telegraph lines were repaired: 3,732 kilometers of trunk lines and 1,639 kilometers of branch lines. Underwater lines are not included. Repairs will continue this year in order to ensure smooth communication.

Cooperation and Convenience: After the establishment of wireless telegraph stations, wired telegraph began to have competition in business, striving for speed in sending and receiving messages and eliminating the bad habits of bureaucratic government offices, making it convenient for people to use telecommunications. National enterprises are owned by all the people of the country, not the private property of the organizers, and should naturally strive to facilitate the people. Wired and wireless telegraph have their own strengths and cannot be abandoned. In European and American countries, wireless telecommunications have been very developed, but wired telecommunications still exist. Currently, there are one or two locations in this city where the sending and receiving offices of wired and wireless telegraph have been jointly established. There is solid cooperation in business. In the future, after the completion of the Transportation Building, various agencies under the Ministry of Transportation in this city, such as China Merchants Bureau, airlines, and international telegraph bureau, are planning to concentrate their offices in one place, which will not be a problem for the merger of wired and wireless telegraph bureaus.

Joint Postal and Telegraph Establishment: The Ministry of Transportation previously ordered the joint establishment of postal and telegraph offices in all third-class and lower bureaus. This city is a pilot area. The telegraph and postal authorities have repeatedly discussed the matter. Since there are 19 postal branches in this city, there is no need to set up sending and receiving offices in remote areas to avoid increasing expenses. In prosperous areas, they are planning to set up sending and receiving offices, but they must also consider whether there are surplus houses in the current postal branches that can be used jointly. Therefore, it has not yet been realized. Recently, the telegraph bureau first added a sending and receiving office in the Shanghai Bank branch in the West Gate, which began operating on April 1.

New Train Schedule for the Two Railways Still Set to Be Implemented on the First of Next Month 160

The train schedule for the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways is usually changed once every year in March. This year, the schedule change is related to the implementation of joint transportation on national railways, which is related to all railways and must be convened by the Ministry to gather representatives from all railways to discuss. As a result, the new schedule was only finalized in mid-March and was announced a few days ago to be implemented on April 1. However, the railway bureau previously received a telephone call from Nanjing that there were still changes to be made. Therefore, yesterday, the two railways published in their daily newspapers the news that the implementation would be changed to April 11. The reporter specifically inquired with the railway bureau and learned that Nanjing again received a telephone call yesterday morning notifying that the new schedule would no longer be changed, so it is still set to be implemented on the first of next month.

The Climate in This City Suddenly Turned Cold 161

Rain and Snow Fell, Damaging Crops

Since spring entered in this port, the climate has changed. Yesterday, rain and snow fell, and it was as cold as deep winter. The Celsius temperature was only 39 degrees. According to the astronomical observatory report, since spring entered, there have been strong winds and heavy rains and very cold weather in the provinces along the Yangtze River. Zhou Zhanyuan, Who Killed the General Manager of the New New Company, Was Sentenced to Death 162

As a Result of the Police Appeal

Li Minzhou, the Cantonese general manager of the New New Company, dismissed Zhou Zhanyuan, a Tianjin doorkeeper and deputy headman, for repeated mistakes (on the 1st of last month). As a result, Zhou used a pistol to kill Li in room 327 of the New New Hotel. Zhou was also arrested by the police and sent to the First Special Court for interrogation and sentencing, where Zhou was sentenced to life imprisonment for murder. The police did not accept the verdict and argued that Zhou's killing of Li was actually premeditated. Therefore, the police lawyer Gan Jingxian listed the circumstances of premeditated murder and appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court. After the Second Branch of the Higher Court concluded the interrogation, the sentencing had been awaited. As reported in this newspaper many times, yesterday afternoon, Zhao Zhengjing, the presiding judge of the Higher Court Branch, along with two associate judges, Lin and Zhou, ascended to the first criminal court and announced the verdict, revoking the original verdict. Zhou Zhanyuan was sentenced to death for premeditated murder. One pistol and two bullets were confiscated.

Chen Zhongxin’s Corpse Examined Yesterday 163

Chen Had a Nephew Currently Studying at a Catholic Church

A Small Iron Hammer with Blood Stains Was Found Near the Body

Chen Zhongxin, a 26-year-old Cantonese man residing in the French Concession at No. 2, Wufeng Lane, Xiafei Road, above the Huaan Western Restaurant, was invited out on the morning of the day before yesterday around 8:00 AM. At noon, he was lured to the upper floor of No. 28, Baoren Lane, No. 697, west of the intersection of Xiafei Road and Masnan Road. The assailant used an iron hammer to injure Chen's head, causing his death. Afterwards, the assailant, intending to destroy the body, eliminate traces, and deceive others, wrapped the corpse in all the clothes and bedding, sprinkled it with kerosene, and set it on fire. The assailant then took the opportunity to escape. The fire was discovered by the second landlord, a Russian woman named Youli Aifu (transliteration), and the waiter Chen Nianshi, who alerted the fire brigade, drove to extinguish the blaze, and found the body. The police transported it to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch Examination Office to await the autopsy. Details of the situation were published in yesterday's newspaper. It is now known that at the time, detectives found a small wooden-handled iron hammer near the body, with the handle covered in bloodstains, and took it back to the police station. They also discovered that the deceased had a nephew, Chen Tianbao, who is 20 years old this year and is currently studying at the seminary in the Tushanwan Catholic Church in Xujiahui. He has no other relatives in Shanghai. Yesterday morning, the police ordered detectives to bring the corpse's nephew, the second landlord Russian woman, the waiter, and others in for questioning. At the same time, they reported to the Second Special District District Court. Chief Prosecutor Chen Beisan, along with a forensic doctor and clerk, arrived at noon to examine the body. They ascended to the court and, according to the reports from Chinese and Western detectives regarding the investigation after the incident, presented the murder weapon as evidence. The official questioned the corpse's relatives and witnesses about the circumstances of the discovery and then pronounced that Chen Zhongxin had indeed died from injuries sustained before his death. Chen Tianbao claimed the body for burial, pending the police's arrest of the murderer to be brought to justice. The iron hammer was kept on file for future reference.

The Loan Office for Fishermen of Shangbao and Nine Other Counties Begins Granting Loans 169

Notice to Fishermen to Go and Register

The Loan Office for Fishermen of Shangbao, Jinchuan, Nanqi, Chongfeng, Tai and Nine other counties was formally established in Songjiang on the 26th. The office yesterday notified all fishermen to go and register immediately in order to start receiving loans. The details are as follows:

Start of Loans: The total amount of fishermen's loans in Jiangsu Province is 2.5 million, which has been fully raised by the office's chief director, Yan Hao, and reported to the Ministry of Industry and the Construction Department of Jiangsu Province for approval. The funds have been entrusted to the Shanghai Guohua Bank for safekeeping in order to facilitate lending. A reporter from the Dagong News visited the office's director, Zhao Enpu, who said that the office was specifically established to provide relief to fishermen. Each county is allocated a loan amount of 50,000 yuan. However, the loan procedure requires fishermen to submit a registration form, which will be verified by the office. Once the fishermen have found a guarantor, they can borrow. These loans are interest-free and repaid in installments. However, those who have not registered and been approved by this office are not allowed to borrow. Furthermore, the fishermen of Shangbao, Chongming, Jinshan, and Baoshan counties have already come to negotiate and have been approved to establish branch offices. For the other five counties, it is hoped that those familiar with the local fishing conditions will come to the office to negotiate so that branch offices can be established and loans can be started.

Notice of Registration: The Loan Office for Fishermen of Shangbao and nine other counties yesterday notified the fishermen of each county: "For the purpose of notification, this office has raised funds to establish a fishermen's loan office with the aim of developing the fishing industry. The nine-county fishermen's loan office has been surveyed and located at Zhongxin Road, Wai Ma Road, Wusong. It was formally established on the 26th of this month and will immediately begin investigating the conditions of fishermen in each county. All fishermen are requested to come to the office quickly to register so that loan disbursement can be opened. This matter concerns the livelihoods of fishermen and the development of the fishing industry. Please do not hesitate and delay, lest you regret it later. This notice is hereby given. Director Zhao Enpu."

A Large-Scale Red Pill Operation Busted Above the Shenfeng Fruit Store on Henan Road 170

Over Five Thousand Six Hundred Taels of Red Pills and Pill Blocks Seized

Raw Materials, Machines, Etc. are Larger in Scale Than Other Places

Zhang Shiliang, Who Trafficked in Red Pills, Was Intercepted En Route

Lu Liankui, the Chinese Inspector of the Narcotics Department of the General Police Station, learned that Zhang Shiliang, a native of this county, specializes in trafficking red pill drugs. Yesterday afternoon at 12:30 PM, he was again transporting a large batch of red pills and had to pass through the intersection of Henan Road and Tianjin Road. Therefore, he ordered Chinese Detective Liu Shaokui, Song Bingzheng, Detective Zhang Yunhong, and Bao Detective Xu Guirong to go to the address to wait. Before long, Zhang arrived slowly and was arrested by the detectives who stepped forward. Over thirty bags of red pills were seized, weighing a total of 186 taels, and taken back to the police station. Under strict questioning, Zhang confessed that the main red pill manufacturing operation was located on the fourth floor of the Shenfeng Fruit Store, No. 437 Henan Road. Therefore, the original team of detectives rushed there and saw a Wufeng Hardware Store sign hanging on the fourth floor of the building. The doors were tightly closed, and no one was inside. The detectives then managed to open the window and enter, seeing that the interior was divided into three rooms. The front room was the office, the middle room was the red pill manufacturing workshop, and the back room was the pill drying area. Approximately 5,600 taels of red pills and pill blocks, as well as raw materials, machines, etc., were seized, the number of which is unknown. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the Criminal Division One Court of the First Special District Court. Li Zhishan, the police lawyer, stated that the manufacturing operation in this case was larger in scale than other operations that had been busted, and even the pill drying equipment was better than other places. Because the main culprit is at large, the police are currently hunting him down. Therefore, he requested a postponement of the trial. Zhang Shiliang confessed during questioning that he worked as a tea boy in the operation, specializing in cleaning. Yesterday, he was ordered by the owner to carry things outside. The rest of his confession was evasive. Criminal Division One Court President Feng Shide verified the confession and then ordered the case to be adjourned for further questioning.

Service from Old West Gate to Longhua to Begin on April 1

Subsequently, although some businessmen requested to establish the business, the Municipal Bureau of Public Works did not approve it because the conditions were not met, and many of the former employees were unable to return to their jobs. The Municipal Bureau of Public Works, considering that the operation of the South Shanghai Public Bus service is of great importance to transportation, decided to take over the operation of the South Shanghai Public Bus service under municipal management. Internal arrangements have been completed, and the opening is imminent. Although the former employees petitioned the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, and the Municipal Party Committee to be employed, they have not yet received any concrete results. Clerk Zhu said that the matter had not yet been reported by the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, and it was difficult to give a concrete instruction in fact. He promised that the Municipal Government would order the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to investigate and handle the matter. The representatives, who had been unemployed for a long time and were forced by their livelihood, requested that they be reinstated in accordance with the previously signed contract. Clerk Zhu also promised that the Municipal Government would order the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to investigate and handle the matter within the possible range. The representatives were satisfied and then left.

An Incredibly Tragic Murder Case 176

How Zhang Zhanggen Died, Lu Linqing is Likely a Suspect

Zhang Zhanggen, from Zhangjiazhai, Beixing Township, Gaoqiao, Pudong, used to be a copper worker in the Wusong Railway Factory and was quite close to Lu Linqing, a fellow worker in the factory. Later, Zhang Zhanggen resigned because he was on bad terms with the foreman, Liu Changshun, and helped out in a copper shop in Hongkou. Lu Linqing was sentenced to imprisonment for political suspicion and was not released until the winter of last year. Zhang Zhanggen asked someone to intercede, intending to return to the factory to work, but before it could be achieved, he suddenly met Lu Linqing in Hongkou last year. Upon seeing each other, Lu asked Zhang if he recognized him. Zhang replied that he had not seen him for several years and could not help but feel unfamiliar. Lu said that he heard that you wanted to return to the factory, is that true? Zhang replied that he had, but it had not been achieved. Lu asked Zhang to find another good job, and Zhang did not mind. After Zhang returned home, he told his wife, Zhang Ling, that he had met his colleague Lu Linqing. However, on the 19th day of the first lunar month of this year, Zhang Zhanggen went to a friend's house in Hongkou, but for some reason, he did not return home. On the 21st, he went to Wusong, and on the evening of the 22nd, Lu Linqing suddenly came to Zhang's house and said, "Your husband, Zhang Zhanggen, went to Songjiang and died suddenly at my house." When Ling heard this, she immediately rushed to Lu Linqing's house in Wusong with her aunt, Huang Zhang. She saw her husband's body covered with a quilt in the bed. Ling wanted to lift the quilt to see, but Lu stopped her from doing so. At that time, Lu said that his fellow workers in the factory had raised more than 50 yuan and had to collect the body. Zhang's sister, Huang Zhang, insisted on lifting the quilt to see, but Lu's family was large, and they were all violently blocked. Until the time of the funeral, Zhang Ling had already fainted from crying. Huang Zhang glanced at her younger brother, Zhang Zhanggen, whose face was as if he were alive, but she found a cyan-purple color below his ears, and his whole body was covered in cyan swelling. She was about to take a closer look, but the coffin was already closed. Lu ordered Ling to transport the coffin back to the village for burial. At that time, the wife and other female family members were ignorant and were oppressed by Lu and did not dare to speak out. Later, after inquiring, she learned that her husband, Zhang Zhanggen, was actually beaten to death by Lu Linqing and others in a premeditated manner. She wanted to seek redress, but she had no money. Until the day before yesterday, because of the sale of the land, she went to the Fourth Precinct of the Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. After the director of the precinct, Zhan Chun, inquired about her husband, Ling thought that there was an opportunity to take advantage of, so she told how her husband, Zhang Zhanggen, was premeditatedly beaten to death by Lu Linqing, and how she was not allowed to see, and how her aunt, Huang Zhang, noticed it, and how she was trying to seek redress. After Director Zhan took the confession, he immediately conducted an investigation and found that Zhang Zhanggen had indeed died unjustly. Therefore, he secretly sent detectives to arrest Lu Linqing and bring him to the precinct. Lu confessed that Zhang's death had nothing to do with him. The rest of his confession was evasive. Considering the seriousness of the case, he was sentenced to be transferred to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Notice on Burial of Coffins Along the Roads in the Third District, Fifth Precinct 178

Director Wang Extends Kindness to Withered Bones

All Families Should Claim and Bury Their Own

Wang Junfu, Director of the Fifth Precinct of the Third District of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau in Donggou, issued a notice because there were too many coffins exposed on the Gaolu and Luxing roads that needed to be buried urgently. The notice stated that it was being issued because the Bureau had repeatedly received instructions from the Public Security and Health Bureau regarding the numerous exposed coffins in the four townships under the jurisdiction of the Precinct, ordering the families to bury them by a deadline. Notifications had been posted and the families had been informed. An investigation revealed that in the Gaolu and Luxing areas under the jurisdiction of the Precinct, excluding the 43rd map area of the Luxing District, which was buried last winter in conjunction with the Municipal Affairs Office under the supervision of the police, there were still no fewer than several thousand coffins exposed. The exposed coffins had not been buried for a long time, and the stench of the corpses, due to being exposed to rain and sun, inevitably spread far and wide with the wind. If burial was further delayed, once the summer season arrived, the weather would become warmer, and there was a deep fear that an epidemic would break out, which would be greatly detrimental to hygiene. Therefore, strict measures were being taken to eliminate hidden dangers. The public was hereby notified that from this day forward until April 15, they must inform each other to have the families bury the coffins by the deadline. As the Spring Festival was a time when agricultural work was not pressing, if any delays were arbitrarily made, regardless of whether the coffins were claimed or unclaimed, the Precinct would supervise the local Baojia heads to hire workers to bury them on the spot without using lime. If the floating coffin was located in a certain place, it would be buried there by digging a hole more than six feet deep. However, the Precinct did not have many police officers, so it was planned to start from the Xigou to Jiebang Dugaolu area on one side, and from Donggou to Gaohang Dajiangpu, Zhangjiaqiao Shangchuan Automobile Road, and Pudong Avenue on the other. First, the coffins on both sides of the road, which were visible to passers-by, would be buried, and then the other remote and desolate places, or the sides of isolated villages and wild shops, and the deep and secluded places in the fields, would be buried as much as possible to complete this task, so as to emphasize hygiene and improve the city's appearance. In addition to ordering the heads of each map area to prepare for implementation without the slightest delay, the public was hereby notified to strictly comply and bury the coffins quickly. This notice is of utmost importance.

Ronglin Warehouse Resumes Work After a Half-Year Shutdown Under Police Protection 181

The loading and unloading of goods at Ronglin Warehouse in Pudong's Nanmatou has been contracted by Li Hongji. The work has been ongoing since 1928 for seven years. Unexpectedly, in October of last year, the warehouse manager, Ling Jitan, suddenly advertised for bids again. At that time, Li Hongji sought to recover more than 10,000 yuan in unpaid wages from the warehouse, which led to a dispute. The Social Bureau intervened to mediate, resolving to abolish the contract system but allowing the original workers to continue working and signing a draft agreement. Details were previously reported in this newspaper. When the Chunhe ship officially started work on December 13th, the warehouse paid 4 jiao and 6 fen per ton. However, for the second and third shipments, the warehouse only paid 3 jiao and 8 fen per ton. As a result, the workers protested en masse. At the same time, Li Hongji pursued the more than 10,000 yuan in unpaid wages, further escalating the dispute. The warehouse was forced to petition the Social Bureau to suspend work and invited Xie Peide, General Manager of the Yitaixing Nan Warehouse, to mediate. The two sides agreed on a number of conditions, and the warehouse then extended Xie's term as Ronglin's agent and scheduled to resume work on the fifth day of the first lunar month this year, but the results have not yet been implemented, and the warehouse has been shut down to this day. At about 7:00 a.m. yesterday morning, the warehouse suddenly petitioned the Public Security Bureau, saying that troublemakers were preventing the resumption of work. Bureau Chief Wen, according to the petition, immediately ordered Yuan, the captain of the Second Brigade of the Police Corps, to lead a number of armed policemen to protect the resumption of work. The warehouse then hired more than 200 workers from various places and began work. Upon hearing the news, Li Hongji immediately sent a representative, Qiu Xin, along with more than a dozen workers to Captain Yuan to explain the situation. The captain said that Qiu's statement seemed reasonable, but he was under orders from his superiors to protect the resumption of work, and he should obey the order. As for the wage dispute, he was instructed to appeal to higher authorities. It is reported that Li Hongji has decided to request relief from the Municipal Government and the Municipal Party Headquarters.

Reading Q&A

"The Uselessness of Calligraphy" 197

丨Reply to Mr. Wang Zuming丨

In many reading plans sent in by readers, we see "calligraphy" as an item, taking up a lot of time. We also read at the beginning and end of readers' letters how readers humbly admit their "calligraphy" is not good, repeatedly asking for our forgiveness. In fact, these letters are all written very neatly, even the editor's painstaking efforts cannot write like that. This indeed shows how much readers value calligraphy. They sincerely want to learn it, listing it as an important subject, taking up half of their self-study time? For example, Mr. Wang Zuming is a shop assistant, with only two hours of spare time each day. His self-study course is one hour of reading and one hour of writing. Because he is practicing large characters, he also needs to grind ink before "writing". However, Mr. Wang does not have this time. His only solution is to use the hour of reading to grind ink while reading. In this way, it is clear that the focus is on "writing" that "Magu Altar", and the efficiency of reading will naturally decrease.

We are not surprised by this phenomenon, nor do we object to everyone being able to write beautiful characters. We know that there are other reasons for this trend, and we cannot blindly agree with or oppose it.

However, spending a lot of time on writing is always a pity, and it is also the most uneconomical plan for amateur self-study. Since you have unconsciously raised this question to us, we naturally cannot remain silent and must treat it as a serious issue and bring it to everyone's attention.

"Writing" has always occupied a very important position in the eyes of the Chinese. On the one hand, it is a subtle trick for the rulers to wear down the energy of intellectuals, making them forget more important "national affairs" in this small skill, just like women's foot binding, which makes them lose their resistance. On the other hand, it is because Chinese characters do not get rid of pictograms, calligraphy has become a kind of art, becoming a personal enjoyment for the literati and officials, and a sustenance for "cultivating the mind". It can indeed be said that it occupied a considerable position in feudal art.

In the past twenty years, the status of calligraphy has gradually declined. This is a natural trend. Although writing is still listed as a subject in today's primary schools, its purpose is clearly different from before. We no longer have the leisure to waste on this "art" because there are too many things we need to know, which are much more important than writing.

However, despite this, society still retains a fascination with this "art". This is a conservative mentality, especially in places like "government offices" and the business world, where they still pay attention to the handwriting of low-level staff and maintain the concept of valuing calligraphy, which forms the basis of an important item in the reading plans of many of our readers. As for new-style large companies, they are increasingly using typewriters, and even employees are using pencils for daily use, and they don't pay much attention to calligraphy.

Chinese calligraphy will inevitably become an unimportant skill as social life becomes increasingly complex. As long as it is clear, easy to recognize, and quick to use, it is enough. The only people who truly enjoy it as an art are probably people like Zheng Xiaoxu? The above said a lot of idle words, but it is not completely useless for you. You inevitably have unclear understanding in your concepts, and you are still wasting time on this course that does not require much effort. Although we want to protest, if we do not liberate you from the conceptual aspect, we are afraid that we will not be able to convince you!

For the needs of your work, you can practice writing in your reading notes, correspondence, and shop duties. It is really not worth spending half of your time specifically practicing writing! According to our experience, there is no need to write "Magu Altar" characters in stores now, and skilled skills are enough.

There is much more knowledge that is more important than this "calligraphy" and more closely related to your life. As mentioned earlier, there is really a lot of it. Speaking of business, can you all understand the phenomena in today's market? Can your abilities cope with it easily? Can these aspects be dealt with by someone who can only write a good hand?

Finally, we hope that readers who list writing as an important subject will quickly change their views, make some revisions to their reading plans, reduce writing time, and add the subjects you need more, and don't waste your time.

In addition, for all of you who ask about "calligraphy", such as asking: "Is it better for me to learn Yan style or Liu style?" or "Should I copy inscriptions or 'trace帖'?" and "How to increase the effectiveness of calligraphy learning?" etc., the editor will not answer them in the future, because the editor believes that this is not the knowledge that everyone needs, and the editor personally does not have as much knowledge in this area as Zheng Xiaoxu and others. I don't want to talk about it myself, and I don't dare to talk about it either.

Chunqiu

I Have a Few Words to Say (Part 1) 198

— Shou Juan

In this day and age, everything has to change. Some turn to the right; some turn to the left; some turn and go straight to the top; some turn and go straight to hell. I, the editor of this "Chunqiu", don't want anything else, just want to turn into the eyes of most readers, and get most readers to say it's good. Then I would be like when I was a child at the sugar figurine stall, turning that small wheel, turning smoothly to a very big and good sugar Buddha head.

How should the "Chunqiu" be transformed? Looking at the position it occupies, it is only a quarter of a full page, just like a small court in the southeast. And it is still occupied by an advertisement in one corner, as if the four eastern provinces were lost on the map of the Republic of China. I ask, with these small positions, how can it be arranged to look good? I thought hard for a day and finally drew a picture. At first glance, it looks like a theater. The title of "Chunqiu" at the high end of the center is like a stage; the two large special positions on both sides are like two large flower buildings; the remaining three rows of ordinary positions, large and small, are like the main hall of a government office, and the long row at the bottom that specializes in "Whereabouts" "World Oddities" and other positions, that is the moon building. Since the style of "Chunqiu" is like a theater, then all the contributors are super-class celebrities, and all the works are signature plays. As for me, I am just a stage manager hiding behind the scenes. Sometimes I come on stage to show my face, but I am just jumping around as an official.

Our original first position often published works like editorials. It is impossible to talk about society without a head or brain; it is inconvenient to talk about national affairs, and there are many obstacles. If we specialize in empty talk without touching the edge, we are afraid that we will inevitably be blamed for the pure talk of the Jin people. According to history, the Jin Dynasty perished because of pure talk, so it is written in large letters that pure talk misleads the country. How can this small "Chunqiu" bear the crime of misleading the country, so I plan to give up this empty talk article from now on.

Since we don't want empty talk articles, then what do we want? Look! It is the opposite of empty talk. We want substantial articles that describe and depict a wonderful fact in economical words. When you contributors write, please do a clean-up campaign for all clichés and all nonsense, and get rid of them completely; each article should be limited to 400 words. After you finish writing the article, please be kind and move the abacus to calculate the number of words in the whole article, and note it on the manuscript paper. Please don't forget it. As for other odds and ends, as long as they are witty and meaningful, even if there are only a few dozen words, we will welcome them very much.

Japanese Pen Shops in Shanghai 199

— Yan

In the Hongkou area of Shanghai, there are several Japanese-run calligraphy brush shops. All the Japanese people in Shanghai buy their calligraphy brushes from shops run by their own people, and they are determined not to go to our country's brush shops as customers. This is because their patriotism is strong, which is very admirable. However, according to Mr. Li, a friend of mine who has been making brushes for generations, the brushes in Japanese shops are not made by themselves, but are sold by Huzhou Shanlian Town, which is famous for Hu brushes. They are actually our country's goods, not their country's goods. I think everyone will laugh when they know this secret.

Therefore, I also thought of something more ridiculous and despicable: There is a famous calligrapher in Shanghai. If you go to his calligraphy room, you will see dozens or hundreds of large, medium, and small brushes hanging on the wall. Each brush has Japanese characters engraved on it. He said that he is used to using Japanese brushes in his life. If he uses domestic goods, he can hardly write a word. Therefore, he always goes to Japanese brush shops to buy or order them, and he is not willing to go to brush shops opened by Chinese people as a customer. Think about it, the brushes in Japanese brush shops are Hu brushes from Shanlian Town, Huzhou. Isn't it ridiculous? And he is addicted to using foreign goods, isn't it even more despicable?

Finally, I hope that everyone will not think that just because the Japanese also sell our country's goods, we will also sell Japanese goods; don't think that just because the Japanese still go to Japanese shops to buy our brushes, I will also go to shops run by Chinese people to buy Japanese goods. I also hope that the famous calligrapher will quickly change that ridiculous and despicable bad habit.

Humorous Talk 200

— Cao Wennan

A Lawyer

A short lawyer went to court to defend his client. Another lawyer saw him and asked him who he was. He answered him. "Ah! How can there be such a short lawyer? I can indeed put you in my pocket!" "You can," the short lawyer replied calmly, "but after you put me in your pocket, your pocket will be much smarter than your head."

The Effectiveness of Advertising 201

An advertising agency's agent tried his best to solicit a female food store merchant for his company. But this female merchant did not believe in the effectiveness of newspaper advertising.

Soon this agent thought of a way to say to this female merchant:

"You certainly know how a hen lays eggs; it crows and crows: cluck, cluck, cluck! ... Don't you see a duck laying eggs? When a duck lays eggs, it hides them and doesn't let people know. But a hen will loudly report to the public that it has laid an egg. The silent duck hides itself without making a sound and doesn't let people know it is laying eggs. What do you see as a result? You certainly know that the demand for eggs is extremely high, and the whole world welcomes them. Look at duck eggs again, there is very little demand for them, and almost no one knows about them. This is the effectiveness of advertising that you cannot deny."

Research on Inkstones (10) (2) 202

— Wuliao Ke

Overview of Duan Inkstones

(Geng) Stone Eyes Former people discussed inkstones, some considered those with eyes to be valuable, while others considered those with eyes to be flawed. Both are biased opinions. Generally speaking, good eyes are enough to attract people's aesthetic interest, while bad eyes are disgusting. If the stone is tender and moist, the eyes must be fresh and alive, which is a good eye. If the stone is dry and old, the eyes must be gray and yellow, which is a bad eye. Good eyes are also considered to be high eyes, while bad eyes are considered to be low eyes. Later people have all advocated this way of discussing eyes. Among the good eyes, the best are those that are round, upright, bright, and beautiful, with five-colored halos up to ten or more layers or eight or nine layers, and the pupils are fresh and alive, which are truly priceless. In addition, it is extremely rare to have multiple eyes arranged on the inkstone, such as the Big Dipper or the shape of a five-star heart. Shi Yin's discussion of stone eyes in the Inkstone Talk is more comprehensive. It is recorded below:

The eyes of the lower rock stone are called starling eyes, the upper rock and lower hole are called parrot eyes, the upper rock and upper middle hole are called rooster and cat eyes (those with pupils in a straight line are cat eyes), and the half wall is called sparrow eyes and myna eyes. The locals distinguish them in this way. It is also said that Duan has starling eyes, and also has crow eyes and elephant eyes. Yellow is called crow, and blue-green is called starling. The eyes are not valued for being yellow. Round ones are starlings and have crows, and long ones are elephant eyes. The eyes are not valued for being long. There are three kinds of eyes. Those with many halos and are refined and clear are called living eyes. Those that are hazy and dull are called teary eyes. Those that are scorched yellow inside and outside are called dead eyes. (Some people also say that those with large outlines are angry eyes, those with blurred halos are cloudy eyes, and those with white spots in the halos are blind eyes. They are all not top-grade.) The Duan people say that the stone is tender, then there are many eyes, and the stone is old, then there are few eyes. Tender stones are moist, fine, and produce ink, so it is valuable to have eyes.

There are also red eyes, round like coral bird eyes, and green eyes that are tight, small, and have no pupils, which are all inferior products.

Former people also said that those with green veins must have eyes, and there are many green veins in waist stones and foot stones. The green veins are also called eye tendons. Then what are the green veins? We carefully study them. All the green and green expressions of the lower rock stone are expressions of green veins. The Duan people call those that do not form eye patterns emerald patterns. The Hanmo Talk of Mr. Inukai Yan Bokudo of Japan says that eyes without pupils and small ones are mung bean eyes, small ones of mung bean eyes are emerald patterns, and small ones of emerald patterns are blue flowers, and small ones of blue flowers are fine dust, goose down, ant feet, etc. It can be seen that the so-called eyes, the so-called emerald patterns, and the so-called various blue flowers, although the names are different, their essence is the same. Bando's theory that the constituent molecules of blue flowers and eyes are all aggregates of diabase (see the previous discussion on blue flowers) is especially sufficient to be a proof for our explanation of green veins.

Four Company Commanders of the Northeast 203

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 26: Generously Expressing Patriotic Sentiments, Forgetting the Home and Serving the Country; Sadly Facing the Jade Mirror, Lamenting My Longing for People

Tian Qing smiled and said: Not only will he pass through Beiping, but he may also pass through Haidian. You can send a letter home by wild goose. Tian Qing was originally joking, but Zhao Ziqiang, upon hearing this, really felt a bit infatuated. He raised his head and looked towards the south where the goose flew, gazing blankly. The wild geese flew up very quickly. By the time he looked at them, he could not see even a black shadow in the sky. On this day, the dusk truly crossed over Haidian. At Zhao Ziqiang's home, not long after they had finished dinner, Yang Guizhi sat in the new room under the lamplight, finding an old sock of Ziqiang's and wanting to remake it for herself to wear. She sat quietly under the lamplight, paying attention to nothing. The flock of wild geese flying in the sky happened to make a few cooing sounds, sending that desolate sound into her ears, which made her heart pound involuntarily. She was also thinking like that, that these geese came from outside the customs. I don't know if they passed through Xifengkou? If they passed through Xifengkou, I don't know how our dear one would be foolishly thinking when he saw the wild geese flying south. While she was thinking, she unconsciously looked out the window and sighed, "Hai!" This long sigh was heard even by Zhao Weng, who was in the main room. But she had been married for a short time, and her husband had left, so the grievances in her belly were exactly Zhao's fault. As a father-in-law, what could he do to persuade her? At that time, he kept it in his heart and did not say anything. When he got up the next morning, he saw that Guizhi's eyes were red. Her eyelids were also a little swollen, which made him even more think that she had not slept well last night. In the morning, he proposed to Jiang that Guizhi was very upset, so let her go into the city to talk to Miss Huang, play for two days and come back. (248)

Short Story

The Sorrow of the Old Yellow Cow (Part 1) 204

— Mingdao

In the severe winter, the old yellow cow that had been raised at home for many years became ill; it was very ill, and even when given rice cakes, it spit them out without being able to swallow them.

A-shui Sheng sat in the house, holding a dry tobacco pipe, smoking it fiercely, and said to his old wife sitting next to him, "Niang, this old yellow cow is so sick, I'm afraid it won't get better. It has been doing extremely heavy work every year, after all, it is old, and it will definitely not be used for plowing in the coming year. If it dies, what will happen? I think it is better to sell it, we can recover some of the cost, and we have to pay a sum of membership money at the beginning of the first month. Although this year's harvest is good, we have reaped a lot, but it is worthless, and we still have to pay the rent for rice. We have wasted a year of blood and sweat, and we haven't made any more money. What should we use to pay the membership money to celebrate the New Year? So I decided to sell this old yellow cow." As he spoke, his attitude was very firm.

Niang was making rope next to him. After listening to her husband's words, she sighed and said, "We can't bear to sell this old yellow cow. I remember that we spent more than seventy yuan to buy it. Didn't I also take my very thick gold rings to the gold shop in the city to exchange for money to make up the numbers? It's a pity that it has helped us for so many years, and it's old; not only old, but also sick! That's right, we are also a lot older! Now, of course, we can only follow your words, sell it, and bring back some money; but next year when we plow the fields, we won't have this old yellow cow that has been with us for so many years, so what should we do? I don't have a second pair of gold rings to collect money to buy other plowing cattle." As she spoke, Niang's face was very gloomy, but she kept making her rope in her hands.

A-shui Sheng took a puff of his pipe, knocked the ashes off the ground, and pointed to Yinbao, who was playing with a puppy in the courtyard, and said, "Niang, this little girl is already twelve years old. Zhao, the head of the village at the bridge, likes her very much when he sees her. He told me that he wants Yinbao to be his family's adopted daughter-in-law. He is willing to pay me sixty yuan as a betrothal gift first. When Yinbao grows up, they will make the decision and choose a day for the wedding, and they will still allow us to go to the wedding feast. I think the Zhao family is a wealthy family. They have a lot of influence in the countryside. Zhao's third son, whose name is Bingsheng, is already fourteen years old and is studying in a foreign school in the local area. He is very handsome. If my family's Yinbao marries him, she will be blessed with good luck. As long as I give Zhao the head of the village a sound answer, I can get sixty yuan, and it will be better to buy a plowing cow. Isn't my idea very good?" Niang said, "It's good, but you actually treat Yinbao like an old yellow cow and sell her?" A-shui Sheng said: I have made up my mind to do this. The old yellow cow is sold to be killed, but Yinbao is sent to other people to have good luck. How can you compare people to cows?" After speaking, he smiled.

After the husband and wife made the decision, the old yellow cow was naturally sold. After A-shui Sheng had eaten his fill, he went out to contact the sale of the cow.

In the evening, Yinbao learned the news that the old yellow cow was going to be sold, and her heart became greatly disturbed. She asked her mother, "The old yellow cow is sick, which is pitiful. Why do we have to sell it?"

It is old, it can't do work, it can't plow the fields, and it is also suffering from illness, it definitely won't get better; so your father is going to sell it, get some money, and next year we will think of a way to buy a new, strong, young plowing cow to help us go to the fields to plow."

"Since the old yellow cow is old and sick and can no longer plow the fields, then what is the use of people buying it?" Yinbao asked, with a suspicious expression on her face.

Yinbao's mother smiled and said, "You don't know that the old yellow cow is sold to people to be killed. Don't you see the stewed beef sold in the market? They are all meat from these cows!"

"Ah! Is the old yellow cow sold to people to be killed?" A look of sadness appeared on Yinbao's face, and she questioned her mother as if she didn't believe it.

"Of course it is sold to people to be killed. It can't plow the fields, so what's the use of raising it? Your father also needs money." Her mother replied.

Yinbao heard this and burst into tears. She stamped her feet and cried, "The old yellow cow is my good friend. I take it out to play every day. It asks me for food, and I feed it straw. It knows me. When it's hot, my father takes it to the fields. It never stops working for a day. Now that it's sick, it will get better eventually. Why are you so cruel to sell it? Moreover, if it is sold out, people will kill it. Isn't it good to keep it at home?"

Tilden and Vines Came to Shanghai and Demanded Rejection 206

Tilden and others demanded 35,000 yuan

Rejected at the Annual General Meeting of the Lawn Tennis Club

The Shanghai Lawn Tennis Club held its annual general meeting this Tuesday afternoon at the West YMCA. Among the cases resolved, the most important was the overturning of the request for Tilden and Vines to come to Shanghai for a performance, because the amount was too large. The goal of Tilden and Vines was as high as 35,000 yuan, so it was rejected and not accepted. Therefore, will the world tennis kings not be seen this autumn? The club's staff has also been re-elected. The resolutions are recorded below:

Reject Tilden's Request 207

The first thing proposed at the annual general meeting was the negotiation for Tilden and Vines to come to Shanghai for a performance this autumn. The amount requested by Tilden and Vines was as high as 35,000 yuan, and the performance period was two weeks. As a result of the discussion, everyone believed that the club's own economic strength could not guarantee this huge amount. If they wanted to raise this amount from ticket revenue, it would be extremely difficult, and the hope was very slim. Therefore, the request of the two was unanimously rejected.

Invite Japanese Players to Shanghai 208

Secondly, Chairman Graham proposed that the club plans to invite outstanding players from neighboring Japan to come to Shanghai for a performance. The purpose is twofold: first, to improve the level of local tennis, and second, to obtain considerable subsidies for the club's own finances.

Inter-Port Players and Prizes 209

The qualifications of inter-port players were discussed again. In order to avoid various complications and difficulties, players representing the port must reside in the local area for more than three months before they can be appointed. Again, regarding trophy prizes, in order to save expenses, the club's trophies will be changed to those purchased on order from now on, and the winners will be awarded with extremely small prizes.

Results of the Re-election of Staff 210

As a result of the re-election of staff, Graham was re-elected as president, Shen Siliang and Grobas were re-elected as vice presidents, Secretary De Huili resigned, and Shi Ke continued. The following were elected as members of the five committees: Mei Hams, George, Tao Peng, Okamoto, Mo Que.

Announcement of Basketball Schedule for the Middle School Sports Federation 213

Twenty Schools Participate, Divided into "Zhong" and "Ti" Groups

The annual joint basketball competition, organized by the Shanghai Middle School Sports Federation, had its competition rules discussed and schedule drawn by the Basketball Committee of the Federation at a meeting held at the Association the other afternoon. The details are recorded below:

(1) Group Division: A total of twelve schools have registered to participate in the league, divided into the "Zhong" and "Ti" groups. The "Zhong" group consists of six schools: Jinan, Daxia, Chizhi, Nanshang, Fuzhong, and Guanghua. The "Ti" group consists of six schools: Fushi, Minli, Pudong, Hujiang, Shangzhong, and Yuqing.

(2) System: Both groups will play in a single round-robin format. The winners of each group will then compete in a final to determine the championship.

(3) Rules: The competition rules will follow the latest basketball rules published by the National Sports Advancement Association. However, the game duration will be thirty-two minutes (sixteen minutes per half), with an eight-minute break. The same rules apply for the final.

(4) Location: The games will be held at the China Basketball Hall.

(5) Referees: The Shanghai China Sports Referees Association will be invited to officiate. The referees' transportation expenses will be shared by both teams.

(6) Forfeiture: If a team fails to appear on the court within ten minutes of the scheduled time, it will be considered a forfeit.

(7) Postponement: It is preferred that no school requests a postponement to ensure the competition concludes on schedule. If there are genuinely unavoidable circumstances requiring a postponement, a request must be submitted to the Chairman Committee three days in advance and approved by the opposing team. However, all postponed games must be completed before the end of April.

(8) Rosters: Schools that have not yet submitted their player rosters must submit them to Chairman Committee Jiang Jingnan (Guanghua University, Daxilu) before the game. Schools that have not yet paid their membership fees must pay them to Treasurer Chen Bingde before the game; otherwise, they will not be allowed to participate in the competition.

(9) Player Cards: All players must present their player cards issued by the Federation to enter the court. Other students who wish to watch must purchase tickets.

(10) Staff: The staff serving on-site each day will be assigned by the Basketball Committee on a daily basis. However, each school participating in a game may each send one person to serve as recorder and timekeeper. The competition schedule is as follows:
