Movie Special

Details of the Rasputin Case (Part 1) 302

— Cang Sang

MGM Sued for Insinuation

Former Russian Grand Duchess Seeks Compensation for Losses

The former Russian royal family sued in the British court because the film "Rasputin" insulted the princess, demanding that MGM compensate for losses of £25,000. This case caused a sensation for a while, and this publication has also published simple information. This case is not only an important event in the film industry, but also a major public case in history, so the details are recorded as follows.

Rasputin was a demon in Russia during the European War. The name of the film is "The Mad Monk Rasputin." The silent film was shown in Shanghai, and the sound film starred the Barrymore siblings. It was originally scheduled to premiere at the Grand Theater, but it was abandoned for fear of causing trouble with White Russians. The plaintiff in this case is Princess Irina, the niece of the former Russian Tsar, and the wife of Prince Youssoupoff, who lives in Paris. The plaintiff's accusation is that Princess Natasha in the film insinuates her. The defendant, MGM, refuted that Natasha was just a fictional object and had nothing to do with Princess Youssoupoff. After the trial began, the jurors reviewed the content of the film.

Princess Irina is the only surviving member of the former Russian royal family. Her mother is now in England and is the sister of the deceased Tsar. Her father was one of the grand dukes and a nephew of the Tsar. Prince Youssoupoff is also a rare survivor of the former Russian royal family. His ancestors were Tatar kings before being conquered by Russia and owned vast estates before the revolution. The prince and princess were married in 1914. They both testified when the case opened.

This film depicts Rasputin's history in the early years of the Great War. Prince Youssoupoff hated his evil deeds in the court and killed him, thinking it was his duty to remove the violence from the Russian people. Therefore, this film is actually a tragedy, involving the Tsar, the Empress, and the Crown Prince. The love scene is said to involve suspicion of the princess. The script begins with the 30th anniversary celebration of the Romanov dynasty in the Moscow court in 1913. Princess Irina announced her engagement to Prince Youssoupoff at this grand banquet. In 1914, they held a grand wedding in front of the Emperor.

Unexpectedly, after the wedding night, the European War broke out, and Rasputin appeared. He was originally a peasant with some sorcery, so people regarded him as a monk. He was extremely rude and used sorcery to make money. Coincidentally, the young Crown Prince suffered from a strange disease that no one could cure. The Empress loved him very much, so she was very anxious. Famous doctors from all over Europe were summoned, but the Crown Prince still bled and was in critical condition. Rasputin obtained a secret recipe in Tibet, claiming that he could cure it. He later cured him, so the Empress was grateful and kept him in the palace. The Prince could not leave him for a moment. Rasputin's power in the court was therefore more prominent than the Tsar. The Russian court and the public looked at him with disapproval, recognizing his position as a threat. (To be continued)

Film Review

Review of "Puppet Love" 303

— Cang Sang

“I Am Suzanne”丨Great Shanghai丨

"Puppet Love" is a very rare satirical drama, with profound ideas and exquisite techniques, undoubtedly making it a miracle of cinematic art. After viewing it, one can both burst into laughter and cry out loud. It profoundly satirizes the world's people rushing back and forth in the arena of fame and fortune. To outsiders, it's nothing more than a puppet show. Once pointed out, it's hard not to burst into laughter. On the other hand, being used as beasts of burden until exhausted, broken-legged, and voiceless without self-pity, one can't help but cry aloud when looking back. The key to all this lies in whether one is awakened or not. If one can suddenly awaken, it echoes the Buddhist saying of "the four elements are empty" and "turning back is the shore." Otherwise, one can only be pulled by strings as a puppet for life, living a drunken dream. Isn't everything in this world like this? This film makes one feel the pain more keenly and deeply.

The story of this drama is ordinary, but its artistic success is extremely rare and valuable. I can say with certainty that this is the masterpiece of the talented and versatile Lilian Harvey. The ideas conveyed by this film are profound, but without the singing, dancing, and vivid performance of Lilian Harvey as the protagonist, no one could achieve such deeply moving results. Director and screenwriter Lee Rowland was able to utilize Lilian Harvey's skills, arranging and developing them to a superb level, adding to the elements of this film's success, and his contribution is also indelible. Lilian Harvey and Lee Rowland truly deserve the compliment of complementing each other. It is said that this is Lilian Harvey's farewell film as she is tired of screen life and about to retire. Therefore, director Lee Rowland, pitying that she has always been praised as a red star but is actually just a cash cow for Hollywood, specially wrote this "Puppet Love" drama to express his farewell intentions. Mr. Lee is indeed a thoughtful person.

This film has important value in cinematic art. Now, I will briefly mention a few points to summarize the rest. First, the overall arrangement is appropriate. Because the main theme of this film is to satirize the puppet life, some people are treated as puppets, and some puppets are treated as people. These two opposite scenes are performed alternately, one scene tight after another, one scene grand after another. Those who are treated as puppets, are clothed, fed, and enriched there, depicted vividly. In this situation, the one who is revered as a puppet is a dancer named Suzanne. The name "Miss Suzanne" is repeatedly emphasized in advertisements, on the nameplate of her room, and in people's mouths. And the puppeteer, whose purpose is to collect money, is dressed in a high hat and formal attire, appearing as a person of high standing. His high hat and formal attire are never removed, which has deep meaning. On the other hand, those who treat puppets as people express a cynical meaning. Countless puppets, dressed in formal attire, of various shapes and colors, form a grand sight, which is indeed an excellent negative example.

Second, the transformation of the overall situation is the most profound and colorful. The plot of this film leads to the ultimate ideal of love. What reminds the puppets to start anew is not fame and fortune but love. This point is the most brilliant. For example, "Miss Suzanne" vaguely sees in a dream that a large rope is first put around her neck, and then she is bound all over by a spiderweb. Then, in the magnificent background, there are demons, flames, and night forks. Lilian Harvey then performs her superb skills, trying her best to depict the struggle, and finally throwing herself into the flames. A flash of green light, the scene changes rapidly, turning the living hell into the human world. "Miss Suzanne" awakens to the way of being human in this dream and becomes "I Am Suzanne."

Third, the dialogue is very commendable. The profound ideas conveyed by this film owe much to the dialogue. The playwright's harsh criticism of people's puppeteering in the play is also a successful point. This is limited by space, so readers should understand it themselves.

Review of "Flame" 304

— Ling He

丨丨Beijing Screening丨丨

(1)

Who says spring has come to the world? When I came out of the Beijing Grand Theater, weren't everyone shrinking their necks and shouting cold? "This is winter in spring," I thought.

In this bitter rain and bleak wind, I recalled the impression that "Flame" gave me.

(2)

Flame! This drama title should be so magnificent. As the author declared to us, the flame is constantly burning. Burning down half of the landscape of the Northeast, burning down the prosperity of Shanghai, and even spreading along both banks of the Yangtze River. Millions of victims are fleeing and crying in the flames! They are burned down by the flames, they are destroyed by the flames. But who will extinguish these flames? Who will save these millions of victims? The world is full of people watching the fire from across the river, just like the demeanor of the gentlemen and ladies laughing by the river, as implied in the film. We can only save ourselves, using our own strength, to extinguish these flames, and in the ashes and embers, build our own heaven on earth.

(3)

Indeed, the playwright has a new worldview. He unfolded the future of the national war in an extraordinary way in his work. When A-Gui saw the raging fire of Zhabei, he rang the alarm, he called on the vast masses of laborers who rushed out of the broken houses, and fought for themselves in loud shouts. In addition, he also told us that when the flames are burning down the thatched huts, there are no firefighters and no firefighting tools, so they have to watch the destruction of their own property, and at the same time, they are ridiculed for watching the fire from across the river. But when entertainment carelessly causes a fire in a tall foreign house, it is also a fire, but there are scientific fire trucks to extinguish it. Moreover, you can immediately get a large amount of compensation from the insurance company, and soon you can rebuild a new villa. The flames will not cause them any damage.

(4)

Then, how does director Hu Rui understand this script? Did he grasp the center of gravity of the play?

Obviously, he avoided the important and emphasized the unimportant. He particularly exaggerated the love part. On the contrary, he lightly passed over the aforementioned center of gravity of the play, even using a hesitant tone. This is an undeniable fact. But why does the director do this? Although we will not ignore that people have different difficulties, it cannot but be the most painful thing for artists to make a discount on their own works in order to adapt to the environment. We certainly sympathize with the author's old heart, but he must recognize the author's timidity.

It is said that the original script stated that the fire in the thatched hut was caused by the sparks from the landlord's banquet, but in the picture, we see the carelessness of A-Gui's wife. From this example, the author did indeed automatically delete a lot.

According to Yihua Company, this film is "not cut in size". If this is true, then Chinese films have great hope. Otherwise, the author has cleverly done it to the extent that it is "not cut in size".

(5)

Regarding technical issues, the photography is excellent, and the coordination of lighting is a rare achievement in Chinese films. The camera is also very lively, but some places (such as chicken hearts or nine-pointed stars, etc.) are counterproductive. The acting skills of the actors are also quite commendable, but Hu Ping is not realistic enough when playing the role of a farm girl in the first part.

As for the director's rhythm, it is not proficient enough. I think slow motion destroys the tense atmosphere, and the fire fighting scene should be shorter and faster. If you use slow motion and cannot show calm force, then it is undoubtedly a failure.

The New Creation of 1934 Reveals the Mystery of "Beauty" 305

"Cloud Dress and Beautiful Melody" is the crystallization of the cooperation between Warner Brothers and First National Pictures of America. The original English name is Fashions of 1934. This film will be shown in Nanjing soon. The three major films produced by the company last year, namely "42nd Street", "Gold Diggers of 1933", and "Footlight Parade", have long been well-known, but "Cloud Dress and Beautiful Melody" is far superior to them in terms of famous songs, wonderful dances, and plot. There is an exhibition of new-style clothing in 1934, which exposes the secrets of Parisian fashion art. The ladies and celebrities in Shanghai who love beauty must be eager to see it first.

Film Novel

Carolina (6) 306

— Wen Yin

Will apologized to Joanna very awkwardly. He said his mother certainly hadn't ordered the blacks to do that... If she had known, she wouldn't have agreed... He then asked Joanna to attend the dance. Joanna shook her head and refused. Will said his mother would love to meet her, that his whole family would love for her to come. He begged her earnestly. Joanna felt a little embarrassed because of the flowers just now, as if she was being petty, but Will said he had come specifically to invite her. So, because of his earnest attitude, Joanna knew his words were false, but she couldn't refuse outright, so she agreed.

It was already evening that day. Connerly sat in a large chair, watching pairs of dancers waltzing gracefully. Her daughter, Geraltine, stood beside her. Mrs. Connerly said to Geraltine, "Will is dancing with that girl again." Her voice was low, but filled with suppressed anger. She continued, "If I had known Will was so brainless... I wouldn't have invited that girl Butters... Alas, those flowers were too expensive..." The mother and daughter stared. That slender figure, wearing simple and unadorned clothes, was gracefully spinning in Will's arms, her eyes shining as she looked at Will's face. Once, Geraltine complained to her mother, "It's no use you inviting Jack Huntington. Can't you see he's been chasing after Florentine all night?"

Robert walked up. He drank a lot of cipio made by himself, because he didn't like drinking that fruit water. He asked Mrs. Connerly with drunken eyes, "How's the dance going, the joyful dance?" Mrs. Connerly shook her head and said, "Will is outrageous, he's being so unfair to Florentine." Old Robert said, "That's good for Florentine. Sometimes a man's attitude..."

"A little cold will make a woman kinder." He finished speaking and chuckled. Mrs. Connerly complained to him, "What good is that for Will?" After a while, she looked at Joanna's slender figure and muttered to herself, "She's simply a vixen."

"She's not welcome here." Robert said, "I welcome her, she reminds me of my lost youth." Mrs. Connerly bit her lip and said resentfully, "Unfortunately, Will's behavior also reminds me of... I still approve of your youth, forever buried and motionless."

Joanna suddenly felt uneasy, she had already noticed that Mrs. Connerly's eyes were too stern... Robert's eyes were also a little strange... Will seemed to know her unease, he led Joanna to the garden, where there was a hammock made from the body of an old carriage, suspended from an oak tree with a few ropes. Will and Joanna sat down. He sat beside her, feeling how lovely and respectable she was. His heart was beating. His hand curved around behind her and encircled her fragrant shoulders. He chatted about the past stories of Connerly Mansion, several famous figures in the history of the Civil War, all of whom had been entertained there. Joanna's head leaned back, resting on Will's broad shoulder, she listened as if intoxicated. The night was so lovely... The scenery was so endearing... She felt as if she was a longtime resident here... She was dreaming like this when suddenly someone called Will. (To be continued)
